Current Commentary

Protest Against the Japanese Military Exercises in Pingjin

By Hua

While Nanjing, Shanghai, and other places are celebrating President Chiang's birthday with great enthusiasm, in North China, which also belongs to our national sovereignty, the Japanese military is conducting large-scale exercises. Homes are being occupied, residents are being evicted, and panic is at its peak. The difference between these two situations is what we cannot ignore at present. According to a Central News Agency dispatch from Nanjing on the 30th, the government, because the Japanese military's actions violate treaties and international law and undermine our national sovereignty, has sent a note to the Japanese embassy to protest. This is as it should be. Now, let us analyze the illegality and unreasonableness of the Japanese military's exercises in North China from diplomatic and political perspectives to arouse the attention of the entire nation.

In recent years, neighboring countries have frequently infringed upon our national sovereignty, especially in military actions. The violation of North China's airspace, the intrusion into the Shanghai city area, and the reconnaissance of coastal fortresses and ports have all been protested by our government, but to no avail. Since the beginning of this summer, when Japan greatly increased its troops in North China, the construction of barracks, the opening of airfields, and even the conduct of military exercises in bustling cities have completely violated the restrictions of the Boxer Protocol, and the safety of our people is not guaranteed. However, the Japanese military exercises in Pingjin are the largest in scale ever. According to the Central News Agency, the total number of participating troops is over 7,000, and the area covers the Pingjin-Tongfeng area. It started on the 26th of last month and has not stopped as of today. Such violations of our national sovereignty and disturbances to our people should be stopped by our country with the most resolute steps.

Let us examine Japan's own position. When the United States conducts military exercises in the Eastern Pacific, its scope only extends to the Midway Islands. Japan believes that it is threatened and maintains the most serious attention. When the Soviet Union concentrates a large army of 300,000 on the Far Eastern border to prevent foreign invasion, Japan also believes that it is threatened and demands its withdrawal. In fact, these American and Soviet troops are only conducting exercises and deployments within their own territory, but Japan believes that they contain a threatening nature. Then, what basis is there for 7,000 troops to conduct large-scale exercises in our territory, even targeting Beiping as an attack objective? This undoubtedly violates our territorial sovereignty and threatens our national defense and the safety of our people.

Moreover, Sino-Japanese diplomatic negotiations have reached the sixth round. It is said that there are no concrete results and it is still a stalemate. We do not know whether these threatening exercises are intended to further exacerbate the stalemate or to use this concrete threat to forcefully break the stalemate and achieve diplomatic progress.

In short, from this large-scale Japanese military exercise, we can imagine that the crisis in North China is now expanding and deepening. This matter is indeed worthy of great attention.

Keelung Incident; Anglo-Japanese Friction Deepens; Britain Dissatisfied with Amau Doctrine; Believes it Contains Provocative Nature

(Tokyo) The British Embassy in Japan expressed great surprise at the "unnecessary and provocative" statement made yesterday by the spokesman of the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Amau. According to the statement, which was based on the Keelung accident, Amau made the statement even though he knew that the Japanese high authorities had ordered a continuation of the investigation into the matter. Therefore, it is believed to contain a "provocative" intent. This matter is actually under trial. The British side strongly opposed the statement made by the spokesman that "after the British submarine left Keelung, a British naval flag was found floating on the surface of the water in the port, from which it can be inferred what the condition of the British ship was when it was moored here." As for the spokesman's claim that the extended visit of the commander of the British fleet in China, Lieutenant General Little, was entirely a matter for Britain itself, the British side also expressed its disagreement. (31st Reuters Dispatch)

(London) People here believe that the treatment of three British sailors on the British ship "Medway" by Japanese police in Keelung, Taiwan, was "extremely brutal." The claim made by the Japanese that the British sailors did not pay the fare has been solemnly denied. The commander-in-chief of the British Navy in Asia, Lieutenant General Little, has investigated the matter in detail and can fully prove that the sailors did pay the fare and that a naval officer was present and witnessed it. According to the investigation, when the three sailors were taken to the police station by the Japanese, they were not intoxicated at all. Unexpectedly, after being released, all three were beaten and suffered injuries all over their bodies. One of them even had his jaw broken. The British authorities believe that if the sailors had disturbed order and were drunk, it would not be surprising that the Japanese police intervened, as it was their duty to do so. However, the British Navy believes that the sailors have strict discipline and will not cause disturbances when visiting foreign territorial waters. At present, what the British side intends to protest is the Japanese police's extremely abusive treatment of the three sailors. In July last year, the British protested to Tokyo because an Indian merchant was detained in Changchun and suffered harsh treatment. He was later released after it was found that he had no criminal suspicion. As for the Chinese employees of British commercial firms in Manchuria who were abused by the Japanese police, there are countless cases. Among them, one person died due to serious injuries. This time, the British protested to Japan over the Keelung incident, aiming to demand that the Japanese side provide appropriate compensation to the injured sailors. The British government hopes that Japan can do so in order to end this unfortunate incident. (31st Reuters Dispatch)

(Tokyo) According to a Domei News Agency dispatch from Taiwan, the local authorities have conducted a detailed investigation into the case of the three British sailors being abused by Japanese police in Keelung. All the facts reported by the British side are groundless. This investigation was carried out by the police station after the British consul in Taiwan lodged a protest. According to the Domei News Agency, the Japanese investigation found that the three British sailors hired a car from a certain place to Keelung late at night on October 7th. Unexpectedly, after getting off the car, the three immediately entered a cafe and did not pay the fare. Therefore, the driver reported to the nearby police. The Japanese police ordered the British sailors to go to the police station for questioning. At that time, a British naval officer was willing to testify. However, because the officer's testimony was completely inconsistent with the facts provided by the three sailors, the officer was also taken to the police station. However, all four were released at dawn. The investigation found that the sailors had not been subjected to any abuse. The British side's sudden protest over this incident shows that the British side may have other intentions and is taking this case as an excuse. (31st Reuters Dispatch)

Important Meeting of Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs to Discuss Issues with Russia

After the Iraqi Coup; Military Dictatorship Established; Sidqi is the Leading Figure; Former Prime Minister Flees, Army Chief Executed

Jerusalem After a bloodless coup in Baghdad, the capital of Iraq, yesterday, the country has effectively established a military dictatorship. The figure behind the scenes is General Sidqi, the most ambitious and powerful military leader in Iraq. However, his name is not on the new cabinet list. Well-informed sources believe that the coup in Iraq was caused by disagreements over the implementation of conscription for nomadic tribes. Sidqi wanted to quell the rebellion of the Shia tribes in the Euphrates River basin, and he requested the deployment of troops and prepared reinforcements with combat capabilities for use. Therefore, he advocated the implementation of conscription. However, the government led by General Yasin intended to adopt a more moderate attitude and did not approve Sidqi's proposal. Thus, the coup followed. It is generally expected that the new cabinet organized by Salaiman will implement a universal conscription system. However, the tribes are extremely opposed to conscription, which may cause unrest. Sidqi also advocates the use of brutal methods. It is believed that if the unrest develops, the world will shift its attention to the Arab National Union movement in Palestine. On the other hand, if the Iraqi tribes do rebel, the Middle East may fall into turmoil. After the new cabinet of Salaiman took office, it expressed its willingness to maintain the original friendship with Britain. According to Baghdad sources, the cabinet of General Yasin was fortunate to resign, otherwise the Iraqi army might have come to the capital and dissolved it by force, and a bloody tragedy would have been difficult to avoid. At that time, Iraqi troops were concentrated in Guila Khan, 70 miles northeast of Baghdad. At that time, many army planes dropped many leaflets over Baghdad, all signed by Sidqi, demanding that Yasin's cabinet resign quickly, and claiming that there were many cabinet members who harmed the public for their own benefit. Therefore, the army must expel them. Subsequently, the planes dropped four bombs as a warning, resulting in one person seriously injured and dozens slightly injured. Seeing this situation, Yasin's cabinet immediately announced its resignation. The new Prime Minister Salaiman issued a notice today, instructing the people to live and work in peace and not to be alarmed. Yesterday, shops in the city were closed, but the local situation was still peaceful. It is expected that the big day will return to normal. (31st Reuters Dispatch)

Cairo It is heard that General Yafar, a powerful figure in Iraqi politics, was shot dead in Baghdad today. The general was the former Minister of Defense in the cabinet and a major enemy of the new government. He had been hiding since the violent coup took place. (31st Reuters Dispatch)

Baghdad According to official announcements, former Prime Minister General Yasin and resigned cabinet members Aalit and Said have left Iraq for the benefit of the people. It is believed that the three are heading to Syria. (31st Reuters Dispatch)

Damascus Former Prime Minister of Iraq, General Yasin, left the country for Beirut and arrived here today. (31st Reuters Dispatch)

(London) A coup occurred in the Kingdom of Iraq yesterday, and the cabinet organized by General Yasin was forced to resign. According to news from the British Embassy in Iraq, the coup was not of a military nature. After the Yasin cabinet was forced by its political enemies to resign, King Ghazi Faisal appointed Sulaiman to organize a new cabinet of seven members. Sulaiman served as Prime Minister and Minister of Interior. The political crisis was thus resolved. According to the Anglo-Iraqi Treaty of 1930, Britain had already recognized Iraq as an independent country and was not obligated to maintain domestic security in Iraq. However, if the events develop to the point where they affect British interests in Iraq, two brigades of British troops stationed in Cairo, Egypt, and one brigade of troops stationed in Palestine are ready to move to prevent any eventuality. (31st Havas News Agency Dispatch)

U.S. Presidential Election: Unemployment Problem Important; Roosevelt to Propose Amending the Constitution, Stipulating Maximum Working Hours and Minimum Wages

(New York) President Roosevelt has so far revealed little about his platform for re-election. However, it is widely expected that Roosevelt will issue a surprising statement in response to his political opponent, Republican presidential candidate Landon's, accusations regarding the National Recovery Administration. The Democratic Party members are deeply aware that the repeated announcements by the Republicans that there are still 11 million unemployed people nationwide are having a significant impact. Therefore, it is anticipated that President Roosevelt will continue to formulate plans to encourage employment. To that end, he may amend the Constitution to establish maximum working hours and minimum wages on a national scale. Yesterday, on Wall Street, someone bet $9,000 against $5,000 that President Roosevelt would be re-elected. Judging from the number of registered voters nationwide, the number of voters who can vote is about 5 million more than in 1932, with a total of 45 million. (Reuters, 31st)

Brooklyn President Roosevelt delivered a speech at the Brooklyn Academy of Music today, attacking the enemies of the Social Security Act, calling it a crucial undertaking that the American people will praise on November 3rd. The Social Security Act is a new charter to protect American workers, supported by enlightened employers, church leaders, philanthropists, and educators. Even 67 Republican members of the House of Representatives have expressed sympathy, with only 18 opposing. In the Senate, 15 Republican senators support the bill, with only 5 opposing. Is it not puzzling that you now deny your Senators and Representatives? It is now heard that unscrupulous employers are using money to buy off workers and exert pressure, which is tantamount to exploiting workers' blood and sweat and is not to be taken as a model. Regarding the water and drought relief work relief agencies, officials claim that these agencies not only relieve famine and unemployment but also restore hope. (National Telegram, 30th)

(New York) There is much speculation here today as to whether President Roosevelt will deliver an exciting declaration regarding the National Recovery Administration in his final minute of the election campaign. Former President Hoover stated in a speech in Denver that he had rejected many of the plans proposed by President Roosevelt during his term because they would delay the nation's recovery. Former National Recovery Administration Director General Johnson stated in a speech in Waukesha, Wisconsin, that he expected President Roosevelt to win a great victory. It is still doubtful whether Republican candidate Landon will win the votes of six states. (Reuters, 31st)

Britain Advocates Control of Armaments, Opposes Nationalization

(London) The Arms Manufacturing Investigation Committee submitted a report today, stating that the most effective way to eliminate obstacles to the elimination of private arms manufacturing is to conclude international agreements to limit armaments. It is absolutely impossible to establish a universal national patent system, and it is requested that Britain not consider it as part of its national policy. Methods for regulating and controlling armaments domestically should be promoted quickly. The various proposals recently put forward by the United States in the League of Nations regarding armaments can serve as the basis for concluding international agreements. The various recommendations of the committee are listed below: (1) The government should bear full responsibility for the arms industry; (2) Establish government manufacturing plants to supply the equipment for the navy and air force; (3) Limit the profits of various arms merchants in peacetime, and forcibly impose them during wartime; (4) Arms exports should have more active licensing methods; (5) Stop the practice of issuing public and ordinary passports; and (6) Prohibit private exports of surplus and old armaments. (Reuters, 31st)

More than one hundred schoolchildren were playing in the sunlit streets, resulting in more than seventy being bombed to death. Most of them were bombed into powder. Parents heard the alarm and rushed to look for their children. The scene at the time was extremely tragic. A special correspondent from Reuters witnessed a woman holding a two-year-old girl, half of whose face had been bombed, but she was still alive. Two Scottish ambulances in the Barajas area were also destroyed by bombs, fortunately, the paramedics inside the vehicle were not injured. (Reuters, 30th)

A bomb flew over, and the woman lost her head immediately, and the other three children also died. Only the baby in her arms was safe and sound, which is also a miracle. A total of twenty people were killed in this battle, and many were injured, several of whom were already on the verge of death. (Havas, 31st)

U.S. Seamen's Strike Spreads; Pickets Appear on the Pacific Coast; Atlantic Workers Advocate Responding

(San Francisco) Shipping along the Pacific coast came to a standstill today due to the general seamen's strike. The General Federation of Labor has ordered the organization of pickets. There are now 500 pickets in this area, with 12 pickets stationed at each wharf. The General Federation of Labor also warned 40 ships anchored in the port here not to set sail without authorization. It is heard that pickets have appeared in Seattle, Portland, San Pedro, San Diego, and other ports. The police have sent more than 180 special police officers to the coast to maintain law and order, and there are seven police cars on standby, each carrying two police officers armed with pistols and tear gas. Labor Minister McLafferty still hopes today that employers and union representatives can hold reconciliation meetings. This negotiation was suspended yesterday due to the strike. The union has also organized a strike committee and is willing to consider any possible mediation. Shipowners declared that they do not want to operate ships or load and unload goods, nor do they want to try to break the strike, so serious disturbances are expected not to occur. 800 dockworkers in this area and Oakland have joined the strike, resulting in the closure of warehouses and cold storage facilities. In addition, the labor unrest is spreading further today. Seamen in Astoria, Oregon, voted today to carry out a sympathy strike. Seamen in New Orleans are waiting for official reports from the Pacific coast to determine their actions. The situation on the Atlantic coast in New York is also becoming dangerous today. According to a Seamen's Union official, sailors on American ships in the port will strike. The issue of a sympathy strike by New York seamen is scheduled to be voted on tonight. (National Telegram, 30th)

(New York) The Seamen's Protection Committee recently unanimously decided to strike for 24 hours to express disagreement with the striking seamen in San Francisco and to urge the International Seamen's Union to announce a general strike of all seamen along the Atlantic coast. The International Committee Union is scheduled to meet here tonight to decide. (Havas, 30th)

(New York) At a meeting of the Seamen's Protection Committee today, a vote resulted in a unanimous request for a general strike of seamen on the Atlantic coast to express sympathy for the strikers on the Pacific coast. This vote aims to force the executive committee of the International Seamen's Federation to intervene. The executive committee is scheduled to meet tonight. The labor unrest on the Pacific coast is spreading, and more than 150 ships are idle. The strike committee is now demanding that all ships in the port of New York that are scheduled to set sail within 24 hours go on strike. If the strike continues, at least 20,000 port workers on the west coast will be unemployed. (Reuters, 31st)

The Trend of the Situation in Shanxi Province: A Renewed Vigor Emerges After the Implementation of the New Policies; Strict Prevention of Traitors and Protest Against Japanese Aircraft Flights

Taiyuan Correspondence: Shanxi Province, located in the northwest, is hampered by difficult transportation. In the past, in the domestic political situation, whether in terms of military, political, or economic culture, it did not occupy an important position. However, recently, with the national crisis becoming severe and North China in danger, and as a certain power is sharpening its weapons to invade the extreme west, the situation in Shanxi Province has not only formed the forefront of national defense in the northwest but has also become the center of gravity of the political situation in North China. Therefore, what is the recent situation and what is the trend in Shanxi Province? It is worth paying close attention to. Therefore, a brief record of its situation is as follows:

Vigorously Implementing New Policies

Since the beginning of the Republic of China, all major powers in Shanxi Province, except for the political part where the governors appointed by the central government were in charge for several years in the early Republic, from the fourth and fifth years of the Republic, Yan Xishan served as both military governor and governor, forming a consistent political situation. In the nineteenth year of the Republic, Yan briefly left Shanxi. In the winter of the twentieth year of the Republic, Yan returned from Dalian, and the central government gave him the position of Director of Pacification of Taiyuan, in charge of Shanxi and Suiyuan provinces. Therefore, all facilities in Shanxi Province are still under Yan's responsibility. However, in the political history of Yan, Zhao Daiwen has always been his most powerful assistant. For more than twenty years, without interruption day and night, he personally consulted on everything, big or small, because they shared the same goals and had a very good relationship. This summer, the Chairman of Shanxi Province, Xu Yongchang, resigned, and Zhao was ordered by the central government to succeed him. After taking office, he and Yan jointly urged military and political personnel to work hard together. Among the most laborious and effective measures taken by the authorities in recent Shanxi politics are the following: (1) Civil servants implement morning exercises; (2) Civil servants uniformly change to short clothes; (3) Training all levels of civil servants, county magistrates, personnel in charge of public justice groups in each county, directors of education bureaus in each county, principals of higher primary schools in each county, and high school students in each county. Recently, village chiefs and merchants from all counties in the province will also be trained; (4) Implementing a ban on opium and gambling; (5) Ordering all agencies and schools to hold flag-raising and flag-lowering ceremonies every day; (6) Strictly preventing the activities of traitors; (7) Rectifying social customs, such as female waitresses in restaurants and female barbershops; (8) Severely punishing corrupt officials and implementing the crime of dereliction of duty stipulated by Yan and approved by the central government. The above items are roughly the major points of the new policy, and because of the morning exercises and the change to short clothes, a renewed vigor has emerged from top to bottom. Civil servants at all levels and most of the masses have followed suit, and have all worn short clothes of brown or gray.

Strictly Prohibiting Opium and Gambling

In the midst of vigorously implementing the new policies, Shanxi Province also strictly prohibits opium and gambling. At the beginning of Zhao's tenure, he ordered the chief of the Public Security Bureau, Wei Gengshu Rong, to summon the managers of major hotels and restaurants to be responsible for making guarantees. Thereafter, these hotels and restaurants must never allow gambling, prostitution, or opium smoking to occur. Violators will be punished with the death penalty. With this one order, everything was immediately clarified. As for the opium situation in Shanxi Province, it was indeed eradicated between the third and fourth years of the Republic. Even opium smokers were listed by Yan as one of the three evils in the six major policies between the seventh and eighth years of the Republic, and were strictly prohibited. The ban was carried out vigorously and thoroughly. At that time, every tael of opium soil rose to more than twenty yuan, and it was still impossible to buy. The remaining few opium smokers, feeling the strictness of the law, did not dare to try. Moreover, because of the exorbitant price, where would they find such a huge sum to provide for daily consumption? Therefore, without official prohibition, they had already begun to prohibit themselves. Since the tenth year of the Republic, the authorities have been busy with military affairs, and have adopted a fine method for opium prohibition. As a result, a big gap was invisibly leaked. Although the opium ban has not been completely eliminated, gold pills of various colors such as blue, red, yellow, and gray have been smuggled in from the north from Tianjin and Shijiazhuang, and from the south from Zhengzhou and Luoyang, continuously and secretly. The people of Shanxi initially thought they were opium cessation medicines and took them together. The authorities also did not pay close attention and strictly ban them. After opium smokers had used it for a long time, they became addicted and spread it, spreading wider and wider. Before the opium disaster could be eliminated, the pill poison spread everywhere. Following in the footsteps of the gold pill, there were also the most potent drugs such as noodle flour. According to recent official statistics, the loss suffered by the people of Shanxi from the poison disaster in the past ten years, tangible and intangible, has reached more than 100 million yuan. Shanxi Province has been impoverished and financially exhausted in recent years, and its vitality has been damaged, almost beyond redemption. The cause is here. In the 20th year of the Republic, the provincial government was reorganized, and Xu Yongchang took charge of Shanxi, hating the severity of the pill poison. Therefore, the provincial government specially established a committee to investigate and ban drugs, appointing provincial committee member Ma Jun as the director, formulating separate regulations, and submitting them to the central government for implementation. Anyone in Shanxi who was found to be trafficking in and selling gold pills and noodle flour, regardless of the amount, was executed by shooting. Addicts were also sentenced to fixed-term or indefinite imprisonment. For several years, the number of drug offenders executed by shooting throughout the province has reached nearly a thousand. Since the association vigorously investigated and banned it, the disaster of pill flour began to diminish. At the beginning of the official ban on drugs, after various studies, in order to make it easier to achieve results, the Provincial Government Opium Prohibition Assessment Office officially produced opium cessation medicinal cakes as substitutes. Most of the raw materials for the medicinal cakes were opium soil, and they were divided into three types, A, B, and C, according to the high content. Each piece weighed one tael and was affixed with a stamp. They were distributed to licensed merchants for sale. The authorities originally intended to use this to replace the pill flour and quickly eliminate the drug disaster. Most of the opium soil was transported to Suiyuan and Shaanxi provinces. Now that the authorities' plan to ban drugs has been completed, they have decided to implement an opium prohibition policy in accordance with the central government's opium prohibition regulations. They have abolished the old drug investigation and prohibition committees and opium prohibition assessment offices, and have established the Shanxi Opium Prohibition Supervision Office, with Yan as the supervisor, Zhao as the co-supervisor, and Ma Jun and others as assistant supervisors. It has been formally established and has begun to work, intending to complete the opium ban. The office has now formulated a general outline for the implementation of opium and drug prohibition and measures for assisting the public justice groups in the counties and villages, and announced their implementation.

Preventing Traitors

Recently, rumors have been rife, and traitors in various places have turned restless, especially in the provincial capital and the Datong area of northern Shanxi. In order to strictly prevent this, Shanxi Province has also listed the prevention of traitors as one of the recent important policies. Regulations have been formulated and announced for implementation, ordering military police and public justice groups in each county to be prepared, allowing the people to report and receive rewards in accordance with the regulations. If they dare to falsely accuse, they will be punished for framing. The law is similar to this year's measures to prevent the reporting of communist bandits.

Related to the prevention of traitors is the establishment of special agencies by the Japanese in Taiyuan. Previously, during the period when Shanxi Province strongly advocated anti-communism last winter, the Japanese sent personnel to Taiyuan to negotiate with the authorities and, under the pretext of investigating bandit activities, requested to establish special agencies in Taiyuan and station personnel in Taiyuan on a regular basis. At that time, the authorities, believing that it was only for investigative purposes, only allowed one or two researchers to be stationed. Since then, the Japanese have sent military officers and built buildings in Xincheng Street and other places, secretly posing as special agencies. Subsequently, the number of Japanese coming and going became more frequent, every week on the first and fourth, and there were regular Japanese aircraft coming. A month ago, after the authorities raised objections, the Japanese side agreed to no longer send aircraft to Taiyuan. As for the special agencies, since Hezhi was transferred to Jinan, all activities seem to have temporarily become quiet. As for Datong, because it is adjacent to the Ping-Sui Railway and is located in the key area of the provinces of Chahar and Suiyuan, the situation is more complicated than in Taiyuan. As for the issue of traitors, because Taiyuan is located deep inland, with difficult transportation, and with orderly order, and most of the people are good, there is little room for activities. Moreover, the authorities have listed it as an important policy and strictly prevent it. Judging from the recent situation, there seems to be no cause for deep concern. In addition, the military, police, and gendarmerie agencies in Taiyuan City have added posts on the streets in recent days, and are strictly prepared, hoping to prevent problems before they occur.

A Major Fire on Baiyun Road in Guangzhou: Over a Hundred Shops and Households Destroyed; Over a Thousand Disaster-stricken Refugees

Guangzhou Correspondence: Since the beginning of autumn, fire alarms in Guangzhou have occurred almost every day. A few days ago, fires broke out successively in Xinshengsha in the east of the customs, the Eight Banners Road on the South Bank, Huaxieshan in Henan, and Longdaowei Street, destroying hundreds of shops and households, causing heavy losses to the citizens. Residents have been busy with the aftermath, and the fires have continued to occur in recent days. At 2:00 AM on the 26th, a fire broke out in the Changsheng Paper Shop at No. 1, Section South, Thirteen Streets in Xiguan, spreading to the neighboring Guangxing Cotton Shop at No. 2, the vacant shop at No. 3, the Yongchang Shop at No. 4, and the Yongchang Warehouse at No. 5, destroying a total of five shops and causing tens of thousands of yuan in losses. At 2:00 PM on the 26th, a fire broke out in a household in Changan Street near the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway Station on the East Bund Baiyun Road, destroying more than 120 shops and households, causing a loss of 300,000 to 400,000 yuan, resulting in an unprecedented major disaster. It was found that someone in a residence on Changan New Street near the road was careless in cooking, and in a short time it had become a prairie fire, and the surrounding streets and alleys were turned into ashes. A large number of rails, sleepers, and a passenger car No. 71 on the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway track and the workers' residences at Chuanlongkou were destroyed. The railway bureau suffered a loss of 60,000 to 70,000 yuan. The express train from Hong Kong to Guangzhou could not pass that afternoon, and had to unload goods near the Dongshan Stadium, and passengers had to change trains here before they could reach Dashatou. As for the shops and residences in the Changan New Street area, more than 120 were destroyed, and more than a thousand refugees were displaced. It was found that the residents of this area had moved here from Zengcheng County in the 18th year of the Republic of China. At that time, due to infighting among clansmen, the weak were forced to move to the provincial capital to live together, but unexpectedly, they were again hit by a fire robbery. It is truly a double disaster. Now, more than a thousand refugees have suddenly lost their homes and have to support their families under the ruins with thatched sheds to protect themselves from the wind and rain, or they huddle in the rubble piles, hungry and cold, in a terrible state. Charitable halls in the city have been sending people to distribute porridge and dry food to relieve the starving refugees. In the disaster area, there were more than ten streets in total, and more than 110 shops were burned down. A female body was found in the cremated area, and no less than 30 people were injured while escaping the fire. After being treated by the rescue team, they were left behind. A list of the burned shops on each street is as follows: Sili Sheng Vegetable Shop at No. 1 Baiyun Road, Shengji Shop at No. 3, Shengchang Shop at No. 5, vacant shops at No. 7, No. 9, No. 19, and No. Zhejiang: Opening of the Literature Exhibition; The Opening Ceremony Was Held in Hangzhou Yesterday Morning; The Exhibits from Public and Private Collectors Are Very Rich

Hangzhou Correspondence: The Zhejiang Provincial Literature Exhibition, organized by the Zhejiang Department of Education, after several months of preparation, has collected more than 20,000 cultural relics and treasures from all over the province, which are displayed in the Provincial Library, divided into twelve exhibition rooms. It was originally scheduled to start exhibiting from 9:00 AM on November 1st, allowing people to visit. It was advanced to yesterday (31st) at 9:00 AM to hold the opening ceremony. Representatives from various agencies and celebrities and scholars Ye Gongchuo, Zhang Shouyong, Wang Tingyang, Xiang Lansheng, Yu Shaosong, Shao Peizi, Zheng Wenli, Qian Jiaji, Zhao Huijue, Xu Xinggong, and others, more than 200 people, were present. Xu Shaodi, the Director of the Department of Education, presided over the meeting and read the opening speech. Wang Tingyang, Ye Gongchuo, Zhang Shouyong, Liu Yikui, Pan Boshan, Xiang Lansheng, and others first gave speeches, followed by a thank-you speech by the Secretary-General Chen Xunci. Then there was a photo session, followed by the unveiling ceremony by Xiang Lansheng. Finally, the guests were invited to visit for a week, and it ended at 11:30 AM. The exhibition content includes: (1) Carved books and documents, including the oldest surviving Dou Jieyin Dharani Sutra published in the XianDe period of the Later Zhou Dynasty, discovered in Tianning Temple in Huzhou, the sutra scrolls of Leifeng Pagoda in West Lake, Hangzhou, the Jia Yi Ji printed by the Jingji Shop of the South Chen Residence in the Beimuqinfang in front of the shed in Lin'an Prefecture of the Song Dynasty, the Wuzhou carved Literary Essence of the Three Su Masters, the Zizhi Tongjian carved in Yuyao County in the second year of Shaoxing, the Yinxue Jiwen carved in Qingyuan Road of the Yuan Dynasty, the National Dynasty Wenlei of the Xihu Academy edition of the Yuan Dynasty, and so on, no less than hundreds of kinds of fine engravings from the Ming and Qing Dynasties; (2) Documents from collectors, such as the manuscript of Zhou Yigong's book from the Song Dynasty formerly collected by Yan Jiuneng, and the handwritten collection of essays by Lin Gongfu of Tiantai by Wu Meicun formerly collected by Mr. Qingcai, which can be called a rare treasure in the book forest. Other old books from collectors in Liangzhe in the past four or five hundred years, such as Qi's Tanshengtang, Fan's Tianyige, Xiang's Wangangtang, Zhu's Pushuting, Huang's Shiku, and Ding's Eight Thousand Volumes, up to Sun's Yuhailou, are gathered together; (3) Portraits of local sages, such as the portraits of the seven generations of Wang Wencheng of the Ming Dynasty, the small portrait of Mao Xihe, and the combined portrait with Zhu Zhukuai; (4) Surviving Writings of Local Sages, the collected manuscripts are extremely rich, and the exquisite ones include the handwritten collection of essays by Xu Wei of Shanyin in the Ming Dynasty, and the handwritten Lai Laixuan poetry manuscripts by Qiang Ji and Fu Zhonghuang of the Ming Dynasty. There are also surviving works of local sages, such as the calligraphy of Zhou Yande of Linhai of the Yuan Dynasty, the Meng'an seal inscription of Yu Quyuan of Deqing of the Qing Dynasty, and the painting of Wu Zhonggui of Jiaxing of the Yuan Dynasty imitating Mi Youren's landscape vertical axis, and the landscape vertical axis of Ren Taichang of Ruian of the Ming Dynasty, etc. There are also the surviving works of Yue Zhongwu of the Song Dynasty, and the handwritten true works of Wan Xiaoxian, the magistrate of Linhai, etc. There are also surviving objects of local sages, such as the jade seal of King Wusu of Qian, the daytime inkstone of Mei Hua Daoren of Jiaxing of the Yuan Dynasty, and the surviving jade tablet of Wang Huaibin of Yunhe of the Ming Dynasty, etc. In addition, ethnic revolutionary documents, local chronicles, genealogy. Selected Essays, Old Archives. Rubbings of bronzes and stone inscriptions, etc., are also abundant in quantity.

The Route of the Guangzhou-Shantou Railway Is Determined: Starting from Zhangmutou on the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway, Along the Coast Through Lufeng and Jieyang to Shantou

Shantou Correspondence: The Guangzhou-Shantou Railway was stipulated in the three-year plan during Chen Jitang's administration, and Long Sihe was appointed as the preparation member. The original route was planned to start from Xicun, bypass the suburbs of Guangzhou, and go through Zengcheng, Huiyang, Zijin, Wuhua, Meixian, Fengshun, and then to Chaoan and Shantou. This route would have to cross the Dongjiang Bridge in Huizhou, and would have to pass through numerous mountain tunnels in Zijin and Fengshun. It would take more than four or five years and more than 40 million construction fees to complete. Therefore, since Long Sihe's preparation, there has been no achievement. Last month, Railway Minister Zhang Jiaxue went south and decided to extend the Huangpu branch line, starting from Xicun, arc-shaped around the suburbs of Guangzhou, crossing the Shipi section of the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway with an arch bridge, and going directly to the Yuzhu Fort. Then the Guangzhou-Shantou route would no longer need to start from Xicun. The Ministry of Railways believes that Shantou is the only commercial port connecting to various ports in Nanyang, and the Guangzhou-Shantou Railway needs to be started urgently and completed within two years. Therefore, Liang Yonghuai, the director of the engineering department of the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway Bureau, was specially appointed as the preparation director. The new route has been decided, starting from Zhangmutou on the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway, following the route of the first trunk line of the provincial road, through Pingshan, Sanduozhu, entering Haifeng, Lufeng, Huilai, Puning, Jieyang, Chaoan, and then to Shantou. This route can save one hundred miles of engineering compared to the original route, and has highway assistance, without huge bridge and tunnel projects, making construction easy. According to this plan, it can be completed within two years. Liang Yonghuai has transferred to various sections of the Zhuzhou-Shaoguan Road to inspect the emerging projects. He will return next month to plan construction.

Songjiang: Celebrating Chiang's Birthday

Yesterday was the 50th birthday of Chiang Kai-shek, the hard-working and meritorious Chairman, and the whole world celebrated together. All agencies, groups, schools, and shops here raised flags to celebrate. Agencies (except the court, which continued to work as usual) and schools were closed for one day. Representatives from all walks of life gathered at the New Songjiang Society in the morning to hold a celebration meeting, supplemented by various entertainments such as singing and stringed instruments to add to the fun. The county party department convened local party members to celebrate and have a noodle meal to mark the celebration.

Arrest of a Deserter

Hu Tu, the squad leader of the first squad of the Shui Lai Miao Water Public Security Team, found a man in a gray uniform on the Minnan wheel ship on the 31st. His behavior was suspicious, so he interrogated him. According to his confession, his name was Huang Nianqing, and he was a soldier in the 57th Division stationed in Zhapu. He deserted due to an incident and planned to go to Shanghai, etc. After Hu Captain obtained the confession, he sent it to the Third District Security Command for review.

Suzhou: Closing of the Air Defense Exhibition

The Military Commission's Circulating Air Defense Exhibition was held in Suzhou Park this time. Since its opening, five days have passed. In recent days, students and the public from counties such as Wujiang, Kunshan, and Changshu have come to Suzhou to visit. In five days, the total number of visitors has not been less than 200,000, an unprecedented grand occasion. The opening ceremony was held on the 31st. The middle school student speech contest held by the association was also awarded prizes on the morning of the 31st. The champion was Dai Huiying, a student of Suzhou Women's Normal School, and the runner-up was Tian Zuheng, a student of Suzhou Junior High School. As for the joint air defense exercise of the eight counties, it is currently under preparation and will be held within ten days. Commissioner Qi of the Second District came to Suzhou the day before yesterday to discuss with Deng County Chief of this county and Xu County Chief of Wujiang.

A Teacher in Love with a Female Student Is Detained

Chen Tianyi, a teacher at the Huiling Women's School in Shanghai, was passionately in love with Wang Yifen, a female student at the school, and Wang Yifen attempted suicide by jumping out of a car and was rescued. This matter has been reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that Chen Renyi has been sent to the District Prosecutor's Office by the Public Security Bureau. After interrogation, he was detained pending review. Wang Yifen was injured after jumping out of the car and has been sent to the Gospel Hospital for treatment. Her life is not in danger. However, when Prosecutor Lu of the District Prosecutor's Office went to the ward of the Gospel Hospital on the 30th to inquire about Zhu Yifen's confession, Doctor Wang Lansheng prevented the interrogation and even had a conflict with the clerk. The District Prosecutor's Office will summon Wang Jiansheng for this. Wang's father has hired Attorney Gu En to sue Chen Tianyi for interfering with the family.

Kunshan: Exemption of Rent for Land Occupied by Highways

The Shanghai-Suzhou Highway occupies a lot of farmland within the jurisdiction of this county, but tenants still have to pay the rent in full, resulting in great losses. Local people specially suggested to the county government to exempt the rent for the land occupied and give appropriate land prices to show sympathy. The county government compiled a list and submitted it to the provincial government, which transferred it to the Ministry of Finance for approval. It is now learned that it has been approved to be exempted from rent and taxes.

A Grand Celebration of Chiang's Birthday

The 21st was the day of Chairman Chiang's 50th birthday. People from all walks of life held a noodle narration at 7:00 AM in Dongzhai in front of Ma'anshan, and opened a celebration meeting. The park entrance and Zhengyang Bridge were decorated with colorful arches. Shops and residents all raised flags and celebrated with lights.

Wuxi: Resolution of Disputes at the Vegetable Market

The Wuxi County Construction Bureau, with the approval of the Construction Department in the spring of this year, reclaimed and demolished ten original municipal buildings at the Jixiang Bridge. These were rebuilt into a two-story cement vegetable market, a large project which has now been completed. The bureau requested the Construction Department to send commissioners to inspect and accept the project. At the same time, the County Property Department stipulated monthly rents of two yuan per square meter downstairs, with a deposit of twenty yuan, and monthly rents of one yuan and five jiao per square meter upstairs, with a deposit of fifteen yuan. Merchants were invited to register and sign leases. However, the First District Office, considering the management of the vegetable market to be a district administrative matter, intended to invite merchants to lease through the district and allow vendors from the original Second Vegetable Market on Wanqian Road to move in freely, charging each household a registration fee of one yuan, without requiring them to sign leases or pay rent. This led to a major dispute over the management of the vegetable market. Subsequently, the County Property Department argued that the vegetable market rent had originally been collected by the Municipal Property Management Committee. Since the committee was abolished the year before last, the county had transferred it to the County Property Department for management. Other donations were collected uniformly by the Local Donation Collection Office. The district's unwarranted interference was seen as undermining the entire municipal property, and a special telegram was sent to the Finance Department for instructions. Now, the county government has received an order from the Finance Department instructing that the vegetable market rent should be managed by the Property Department, and the district office should not seize it arbitrarily. Yesterday, the Second Branch of the Public Security Bureau was instructed to notify all vendors to register with the Property Department and officially sign leases and pay rent starting today (the 1st).

Two People Burned to Death in a Fire

At the home of Zhang Genrong, a villager in Qingqi Jigge Lane near Nanqiao in the Third District of the county, a fire broke out around 8 PM the night before last (the 30th) due to carelessness while cooking dinner. A fire was left unattended near firewood, causing a sudden and uncontrollable blaze. Residents in the area immediately rushed to put out the fire, and the Eighth Branch of the Public Security Bureau also sent police to assist. However, the fire was fierce and spread to the neighboring home of Ge Guanjin. Zhang Genrong's six-year-old son and eleven-year-old daughter were unable to escape and perished in the flames. Zhang Genrong himself was also severely burned. The fire was extinguished after burning for an hour, destroying three houses and causing a loss of over one thousand yuan. Yesterday, the bodies of the two children were recovered. They were dismembered and charred beyond recognition, a truly tragic sight.

Lumber Business Robbed at Night

Cai Pinzhi, the Bao trưởng (chief) of the Fourth Bao in Nanquan Town, Hongbi 里, Seventh District, operates a lumber business in Dangkou Town and is a wealthy man. At midnight the day before yesterday, eight or nine bandits suddenly arrived, armed with handguns. They scaled the walls and broke in, prying open two doors, and tying up Cai's family members with thin lead wires, terrorizing them. They ransacked the place, stealing legal tender, jewelry, clothing, and other items worth over one thousand four hundred yuan. As the bandits left, they fired several shots into the air as a show of force. Afterwards, the Hongsheng 里 Watch Post of the Seventh Branch of the Public Security Bureau, hearing the alarm, immediately dispatched police officers with live ammunition to pursue the bandits, but they were not caught.

Nantong: Verdict in the Zhenchang Slaying Case

In Tongyi Zhenchang, Shan Zhigang's daughter, Shan Siru, recruited Cheng Jinming as her live-in husband. Before three months had passed, Shan and her father disagreed with Cheng. Shan secretly conspired with her lover, Wang Jinqing, and her uncle, Shan Zhiyi, to strangle Cheng Jinming, tie stones to his body, and throw him into the river. However, after ten days, the body floated to the surface, causing a great commotion in the neighborhood. The matter was reported to the court. After examination and verification by the prosecutor, the male and female suspects were arrested for interrogation and prosecution. On the 30th, the criminal court concluded the trial, sentencing Shan Siru to death. Shan Zhigang and Wang Jinqing were both sentenced to life imprisonment, and Shan Zhiyi was sentenced to thirteen years of imprisonment.

Suppression of Bandits in Rutaijing

In the area bordering Jiangbei Rutai, a large group of bandits gathered, creating a very rampant situation. The Fourth District Security Command dispatched a team of police to suppress them, and Deputy Commander Peng Longli stationed himself in Huangqiao to command. The area has now been completely pacified. Two bandits who fled to Shanghai, Zhou Quansheng and Chen Dashu, have been escorted to Tong and transferred to the Huangqiao Bandit Suppression Headquarters for interrogation.

Jiaxing: Request to Complete Rice Merchant Registration

Jiaxing rice merchants have recently been found to be smuggling large quantities of rice out of the country. The county government sent personnel to investigate and reprimand them, ordering them to provide bail and to comply with the regulations for the import and export of food in the future. However, the county government had previously notified the Rice Industry Association to inform its members of these regulations, but the date of commencement had not been specified. As a result, various firms had not registered in accordance with the law and lacked the necessary food export licenses. The Rice Industry Association telegraphed Wang Xianqiang, the Administrative Inspector of the Jiaxing District and concurrently County Magistrate, yesterday, requesting forgiveness and rectification. They also requested a clear deadline for completing the registration of grain merchants and obtaining licenses under these regulations. The association is currently compiling and checking grain store registrations.

Gaoyou: Bandits Loot Chenjia Village

Bandits are rampant in Lvyang Lake in the Second District of this county, and looting cases occur frequently. Around 6 PM on the 27th, a small group of thirty to forty bandits suddenly arrived at Chenjia Village on four boats. They looted every household, taking over a hundred dan of rice and clothing from more than ten families, causing losses of nearly two thousand yuan. In order to avoid further banditry, the local people plan to build dams to block the Shenggou Port, cut down reeds, and raise funds to purchase firearms for self-defense.

Locusts Discovered in Taifeng Township

Due to the drought in the eastern townships of this county, locusts have hatched, devouring all the wheat seedlings. In Taifeng Township in the Second District, the early wheat planted in the farmland has been almost entirely eaten by locusts and crickets. The farmers are in despair. If they try to replant, the land is dry and they lack the funds to purchase wheat seeds. They can only sigh in vain.

Ningbo: Passenger Jumps into the Sea from Ning-Shao Steamer

The Xin Ning-Shao steamer, which travels the Ningbo-Shanghai route, departed from Shanghai for Ningbo on the 28th. In the back cabin, a young male passenger, about twenty years old, was seen with no luggage. When the ship reached the waters off Yangshupu, the passenger took the opportunity to jump into the sea and commit suicide. Rescue efforts were unsuccessful. He left behind a letter with the address "Mr. Chen Dongsheng of the Zhongnan Coal Ball Factory across from the Great King Temple, Xinzha Road, Shanghai," and the sender as "Chen Xianghua." He also had a syphilis medical certificate, suggesting he took his life due to illness.

Bengbu: Restriction on Rising Food Prices

The Public Security Bureau of this port, concerned about the soaring food prices, which affect the livelihood of ordinary people and impact local security, convened a meeting of gentry and merchants to discuss ways to stabilize prices. Three resolutions were passed: (1) The highest price for wheat in this port shall not temporarily exceed eighteen yuan per dan. (2) The price of third-grade wheat flour produced by the flour mills in this port shall not temporarily exceed three yuan and four jiao per bag. The entire city must comply, and no one is allowed to increase prices privately. (3) During this period of soaring food prices and scarce supplies, all grain merchants in this port shall temporarily suspend trading with northern grain merchants until supplies are abundant again. The Public Security Bureau has now issued a proclamation restricting food prices.

Chiang Kai-shek's Birthday: Educational Institutions Celebrate Yesterday; Public Education Center Invites Director Pan to Speak; Schools Hold Celebrations and Groups Send Congratulatory Telegrams

Municipal Public Education Center: The Municipal Public Education Center of this city, in order to support the revolutionary leader and admire his special achievements, specially held a celebration yesterday (the 31st), Chiang Kai-shek's fiftieth birthday, to celebrate Chairman Chiang's frugality. In a scope that was not extravagant, the center's staff and the students of the affiliated civil schools, as well as the members of the national art, harmonica, singing, and Peking opera teams, totaling more than a thousand people, gathered to hold a celebration meeting and invited Pan Gongzhan, director of the city's Social Affairs Bureau, to speak about Chiang Kai-shek's revolutionary deeds. Before nine o'clock, Director Pan had already arrived at the center and inspected it. The meeting began at nine o'clock. The celebration ceremony was solemn and serious. In addition to the usual memorial meeting procedures, the attendees offered birthday wishes to Chiang Kai-shek with the highest respect and sang the Chiang Kai-shek Birthday Commemoration Song. After the song, Xu Zelu, the director of the center, briefly reported the purpose of the meeting, stating that the center did not dare to be extravagant and that everything was simple. He said that what we must recognize in this celebration meeting is the greatness of Chiang Kai-shek's personality and career. Director Pan then spoke about Chiang Kai-shek's revolutionary deeds, which can be divided into two points: the first twenty-five years of Chiang Kai-shek's life were a period of filial piety, and the last twenty-five years were a period of serving the country. In this celebration meeting, we should have absolute belief and support for Chiang Kai-shek in order to save the nation and revive the nation. Finally, he cited Chiang Kai-shek's deeds of loyalty and filial piety to encourage the people. The speech lasted for more than an hour, and the audience was very moved. Finally, two students from the center's civil school, Xu Liyang and Xu Lili, spoke about the meaning of celebrating Chiang Kai-shek and why we should celebrate Chairman Chiang, and their speeches were brief and to the point. It was not until after eleven o'clock that the event concluded with a group photo amid loud slogans.
