Details are as follows:

Grand Opening Today

The company has ordered the latest miniaturized film printers, film processing machines, automatic light meters, and other equipment from abroad, costing seventy to eighty thousand in gold. These have already been shipped and technical experts have been hired to oversee operations. Most preparations are now complete, and the grand opening is scheduled for 10:00 AM today. The business department is located at 400 Fuzhou Road in this city, and the technical department is located at 225 Yanping Road. In addition to managing educational films and small-sized positive and negative film reels from various countries, as well as various projection and photographic equipment, miniaturization, duplication, and processing of small-sized films, the company also plans to manufacture projectors, magic lanterns, film splicers, and other equipment. It is expected that products will be available by next spring, aiming to recover lost rights and prevent the outflow of wealth. It is reported that before the opening, the company, being the only one operated by Chinese, has received considerable support from various parties and has already received many orders.

Opening Declaration

Our country's high rate of illiteracy is well-known throughout the world. Now, our government, recognizing electrical education as a powerful tool for promoting social education and imparting knowledge to the people, has allocated funds, trained specialists, and vigorously promoted its implementation. Therefore, the need for electrical education equipment is extremely urgent. Due to the immaturity of our country's industry and the backwardness of production, electrical education equipment still relies on foreign countries for supply. In the past, private promotion has resulted in significant outflows of wealth. In the future, as film education becomes increasingly developed, the demand for foreign goods will increase, and the outflow of money will also become greater. Moreover, it is inevitable that foreign merchants will monopolize and hoard goods. In the long run, this will be a major obstacle to the future development of electrical education. Our company, after a year of preparation, with the support of prominent party and state figures and members of society, has been established. Although it is a commercial organization, its primary goal is to actively manufacture electrical education equipment and assist the government in promoting film education. At the beginning, we will start with miniaturization, duplication, and film processing, and manage educational films and film reels from various countries to meet the needs of all parties. We also plan to manufacture film equipment and all necessary supplies, hoping to prevent the outflow of wealth and facilitate the government's procurement of electrical education equipment, thus fulfilling our national duty to the best of our ability. On this opening day, we respectfully announce our mission to our fellow countrymen, hoping for your guidance.

Scope of Business

(A) Technical Department: (1) Provides film miniaturization services using the latest miniaturized 16mm film printer. (2) Provides services for printing 16mm negatives and positives using the latest printer. (3) Provides film processing services using the latest automatic film processor. (B) Sales Department: (1) Manages famous small-sized positive and negative film reels from various countries. (2) Manages famous small-sized projection equipment, cameras, parts, and raw materials from various countries. (3) Sells adapted and self-made small-sized educational films from various countries. (4) Manages various AC/DC generators, amplifiers, and the China Wireless Radio Research Institute's triple-use machine, as well as various transformers. (5) Manages various educational records and gramophones. (C) Manufacturing Department: (1) Self-manufactures film splicing solutions, reels, boxes, film splicers, and film winding machines for small-sized films. (2) Self-manufactures small-sized projectors and magic lanterns (under preparation). (D) Ancillary Business: (1) Produces commemorative films for various organizations, schools, groups, families, and individuals. (2) Repairs electrical education equipment and radio receivers. (3) Publishes, edits, and manages electrical education publications from various countries. (4) Plans the construction of film studios of various sizes and undertakes educational film mobile screening services. (5) Trains electrical education personnel.

Coarse Grains Industry Association Sends Letter to Local Associations Regarding Food Regulation; Requests Transmission by Telegram to Authorities to Revoke Provincial Bans; Zhejiang Rice is Allowed to Ship After Guarantee and Continues to Arrive in Shanghai

Following Gu Xinyi, Chairman of the Coarse Grains Industry Association, presenting a petition to the Ministry of Industry of the Executive Yuan in Nanjing the night before, the association sent another letter to local associations yesterday morning outlining the reasons why banning the export of grain from provinces is inappropriate, requesting that it be forwarded to the authorities to revoke the provincial bans. The rice boats detained in Jiaxing, Pinghu, Jiashan, and other places in Zhejiang have all been released after guarantees and are now arriving in Shanghai successively. Therefore, the food supply for Shanghai citizens is not affected, and prices are stable and have not risen sharply. The details are as follows:

Letter to Local Associations

Having read in the newspaper that the Jiangsu Provincial Government has resolved to strictly prohibit the export of food grains, and having received reports from colleagues that the Zhejiang Provincial Government has already ordered all counties to implement the seizure and prevention of rice shipments and prohibit the export of rice grains across provinces, if each province acts on its own and bans the export of rice grains, it will inevitably cause panic among the people regarding food. This is because some regions are fertile and others are barren, and production varies. If provinces successively prohibit exports, regions with surplus rice grains will have an excess, and prices will fall, while regions lacking rice will suffer from a shortage and be helpless. The ancients valued the importance of food to the people, and the meaning of transferring grain was of utmost importance. Therefore, our association has deep concerns about the strict prohibition of exporting food grains from provinces. We hereby present a summary of the reasons why it is inappropriate to prohibit the export of food grains from provinces, and we earnestly request your consideration and forwarding to the government authorities to revoke the ban and withdraw the order so that domestic food grains can still be handled in accordance with the clear order of the central government in November 1932 regarding the circulation of domestic rice grains, so as to regulate food supply and avoid famine. We hereby present our humble opinions as follows: Our government is currently promoting rural economic development and regulating the national food supply, which are the only policies for the rejuvenation of China. The government has already promulgated clear orders for the circulation of domestic grains. Now, if we prohibit exports from provinces, it is a self-defeating action and not a sincere effort to balance surpluses and deficiencies and care for the food supply of the whole people. This is the first reason why it is inappropriate to prohibit exports from provinces. Our country is fortunate to have a bountiful harvest this year. However, there are many provinces that rely on neighboring provinces for assistance. If one province prohibits exports, and another province suffers from a shortage of food, it is a hidden worry like Wu and Yue looking at each other. This is the second reason why it is inappropriate to prohibit exports from provinces. If it is said that we must strictly prohibit exports abroad in order to strengthen national defense and prevent assisting the enemy, our colleagues have already recognized this and the Coarse Grains and Oil Cake Industry Association has resolved to propose recommendations that have been submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau of the Municipal Government for consideration and implementation. Domestic circulation should be promoted so as to regulate the food supply. If exports from provinces are prohibited and passports are required for transportation, it is feared that cunning people will take the opportunity to engage in activities and create illicit funds, which is unbearable for the people. This is the third reason why it is inappropriate to prohibit exports from provinces. Rural areas deeply fear bankruptcy. Fortunately, this year's rice grain harvest is slightly better, and there may be hope for recovery. Now, the prohibition of exports from provinces by Zhejiang and Jiangsu will cause the rural areas in the surplus rice areas to suffer from an excess of rice grains and low prices, which will harm farmers. The deficit provinces will inevitably suffer from rice shortages. This matter concerns the people's livelihood and is not a trivial matter. This is the fourth reason why it is inappropriate to prohibit exports from provinces. Provinces governing themselves and counties governing themselves are the corrupt policies of the warlord era, and there is no need to hide it. Now is the time for the government to work hard and renew itself with the people. Regardless of provinces or counties, there should be no divisions and everyone should be treated equally. This is the fifth reason why it is inappropriate to prohibit exports from provinces. Shanghai is not a rice-producing region and has always relied on neighboring provinces for food supply. Now that neighboring provinces are prohibiting exports, the sources of supply to Shanghai are gradually decreasing. The daily food consumption of more than three million people in the city depends on the supply from producing areas. Without this supply, not only will there be panic about food, but the security situation will also be greatly affected. This is the sixth reason why it is inappropriate to prohibit exports from provinces. In summary, our representatives dare not remain silent and hereby present our opinions. We earnestly request your association to consider and immediately telegraph the authorities to revoke the ban so as to maintain the food supply of Shanghai citizens. We would be immensely grateful. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Local Association by representatives of the Coarse Grains and Oil Cake Industry Association, Gu Xinyi, Zhu Zixiang, Yan Xiaoxiang, Cai Yukun, and Chen Ziyi.

Municipal Government Approval

Shanghai Municipal Government Approval No. 4158. The original presenter, Shanghai Coarse Grains and Oil Cake Industry Association, presents a document regarding the prohibition of the export of food grains by Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, requesting that it be forwarded for release in order to maintain the food supply of the people. The contents are noted. A telegram has been sent to the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. Please be informed. This approval is dated October 30, 1936, by Mayor Wu Tiecheng.

Numerous Shipping Accidents Reported on the Yangtze River; Tonghua Runs Aground Twice

The state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Tonghua vessel, currently sailing on the Shanghai-Hankou route due to the congestion of cargo on the Yangtze River, was fully loaded with grain from Hankou and scheduled to arrive in Shanghai yesterday. However, when the vessel arrived at the entrance of the waterway at Wusongkou, due to heavy fog in the morning, the pilot, for cautious navigation, was sailing closer to the waterway when the tide suddenly dropped significantly, and the water depth there was only eight feet. The Tonghua ran aground. The shipowner immediately telegraphed Shanghai for assistance. However, before long, the afternoon tide rose significantly, and the Tonghua automatically floated out of the shallows. The Shanghai Bureau was relieved to receive the telegram reporting that the vessel had floated free. However, at 2:45 PM, the Bureau received a third urgent telegram from the Tonghua stating that the vessel had run aground a second time opposite the Lion Grove Fort at Wusongkou. The water depth there was nine feet, but the Tonghua's draft was fifteen feet nine inches, causing it to become deeply embedded in the seabed and unable to move. The Bureau was requested to immediately dispatch a large tugboat with three barges to Wusongkou to unload the cargo onto the barges and send it to Shanghai first, and then attempt to tow the vessel. Upon receiving the report, the Bureau dispatched the tugboat and barges as requested at 6:00 PM yesterday, ordering them to unload the Tonghua's cargo by 3:00 AM this morning and then attempt to tow the vessel.

Huangpu River in Tow

The Taikoo Company's Yangtze River vessel Huangpu left Shanghai at 2:00 AM on the 29th. That evening, when passing the Jiaoshan section of the Yangtze River in Zhenjiang, the water level dropped significantly. Huang Youzhi, the shipowner of the Jiangxin vessel, had previously reported this and asked the navigation industry to pay attention. The grounding of the Huangpu vessel occurred at Crossing Baouy, where the water flow is turbulent and there are hidden reefs. Due to the receding water, these obstacles were preventing navigation. The Huangpu immediately raised a red light for help. The Jiangxin vessel passed by but, because it was heavily loaded and had a deep draft, did not dare to tow the Huangpu. Instead, it reported the incident to the Zhenjiang Customs and telegraphed the Shanghai Bureau, informing the Taikoo Company. Upon receiving the report, Taikoo immediately telegraphed its Yangtze River vessels that were en route, ordering them to rush to the scene to tow the Huangpu. If the vessel could not be freed quickly, the passengers would be transferred to other vessels going upstream and the cargo would be unloaded. Fortunately, the tides have been relatively high recently, making rescue easier.

Huiping Runs Aground and is Damaged

The captain of the Huitong Steamship Company's Huiping vessel telegraphed yesterday, stating that the Huiping had loaded cargo in Andong and was sailing to Dalian when it ran aground near the newly built Marus Lighthouse in Dadonggou due to the receding tide. The vessel's coal bunker deck and other parts were damaged. The Huiping line in Shanghai received the news and informed the insurance company. Further details of the grounding and damage assessment are awaiting a detailed report from the ship.

Hongxing Labor Dispute Resolved; Work Resumed Yesterday; Months of Stalemate Now Concluded

According to the Dagong News Agency, all the workers of the Hongxing Hosiery Factory at 221 Caishi Road in the French Concession initiated the organization of a labor union in May of this year. Due to disagreements with the factory management, disputes arose repeatedly, and no resolution was reached. Currently, labor and management have filed lawsuits against each other. Although the initial trial has been judged, the labor side is not satisfied and is still appealing. The second labor strike, which began on September 9th, has lasted for two months. Now, both labor and management believe that the prolonged dispute is not beneficial to society. Therefore, in accordance with the Social Affairs Bureau's instructions, with the exception of worker Wang Xiuying, who is temporarily suspended from returning to work, all other workers have returned to the factory to resume work in stages from the 28th to yesterday. The labor dispute, which lasted for four to five months, has finally been completely resolved.

Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Society Establishes Rickshaw Puller Insurance; All 40,000 Members Insured; Deaths Account for the Majority of Claims

Labor insurance has been practiced in European and American countries for a long time, and its grand scale has long been praised by the general public. Looking back at our country, it is still not very common, which is regrettable. However, the Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Society of the Public Concession in this city began to offer rickshaw puller insurance on Labor Day (May 1st) of this year. Claims are paid quickly, and the results are remarkable, truly pioneering labor insurance in our country. Moreover, its scale is quite large, with more than 41,000 insured, making it the largest in the Far East. It can serve as a reference for those in our country who are enthusiastic about social welfare. Excerpts are provided below:

Organization

The Society originally had a mutual aid department specifically for the relief of rickshaw pullers in the event of death or disability. However, to strengthen the protection of rickshaw pullers, a Member Insurance Department was established on May 1st of this year, with a resolution to allocate 30,000 yuan of funds to establish an Insurance Committee. The Board of Directors appointed Zhu Maocheng, Ke Ganchen, Lu Weili, Yan Chengde, Qiu Zitong, Han Yushan, He Wushan, and Gu Zhiling as members, with Zhu Maocheng serving as chairman and Yan Chengde serving as accountant, all on a voluntary basis. The position of manager is concurrently held by Zhang Dengying, the Secretary-General of the Society, who also does not receive additional salary. Therefore, the expenses of the department are very economical.

Methods

As for the insurance methods, it has been stipulated that for all registered rickshaw pullers, the insurance compensation for each person is 40 yuan in national currency. Those who die for any reason (excluding those who commit a capital crime) or who lose both limbs, both hands, or both feet, or one foot and one hand, or who become blind in both eyes, or who become blind in one eye and permanently disabled in one hand or one foot due to accidental danger or other reasons, will receive full compensation. Those who become blind in one eye or permanently disabled in one hand or one foot due to accidental danger or other reasons will receive half the compensation. Moreover, compensation is paid extremely quickly, and must be paid within 24 hours whenever possible. According to the person in charge of the Society, since the insurance was launched, as of the end of September this year, there have been 112 cases of compensation, with a total payment of less than 5,000 yuan in national currency.

Analysis

According to the Society's analysis, deaths accounted for the largest majority of all 112 compensation cases, with 107 cases, accounting for more than 95%. There were only nine disability cases. Among the deaths, endemic diseases, epidemics, and infectious diseases accounted for the largest number, with 59 people, including typhoid fever (13 people), relapsing fever (6 people), malaria (5 people), dysentery (6 people), respiratory tuberculosis (16 people), influenza, gastric disease, meningeal and central nervous system tuberculosis, and tertiary syphilis (1 person each). Common cancers accounted for 6 people, including liver and stomach cancer and malignant tumors (2 people), peritoneal, intestinal, and rectal cancer, and other malignant tumors (1 person). Chronic rheumatism, osteoarthritis, and gout (2 people). Beriberi (1 person). Circulatory system diseases (4 people), including angina and other heart diseases (2 people). Respiratory diseases (8 people), including throat disease (1 person), pneumonia and asthma (2 people each), bronchitis (2 people), and other respiratory diseases (1 person). Digestive system diseases (18 people), of which diarrhea and enteritis accounted for 12 people, stomach diseases (4 people), and other digestive system diseases (2 people). Non-venereal diseases of the urinary system (1 person). Among the 107 rickshaw pullers who died, the age group of 45 to 49 years old was the largest, with 23 people, followed by 40 to 44 years old (19 people), 25 to 29 years old, and 30 to 34 years old (13 people each), 35 to 39 years old and 50 to 54 years old (12 people each). On average, most were around 40 years old, accounting for two-thirds of the total. Based on this calculation, each rickshaw puller can survive to be 43 years old, which shows a glimpse of the life of a rickshaw puller.

Lawyer Wu Zhijian Begins Practicing Law

Lawyer Wu Zhijian, from Fenghua, Zhejiang, is a graduate of the first class of Shanghai University, a Master of Arts from Shijia Gequan University in the United States, and a researcher at the Teachers College of Columbia University. After returning to China in the eighth year of the Republic, he successively served as a professor at Fudan University, a negotiator at the Nanjing Customs Supervisor's Office, and founded the Shanghai Baptist Church of the North, the China Leprosy Relief Association, and China's greatest leprosy sanatorium. He has been hired as a director of Nanjing University, Shanghai University, the Shanghai YMCA, the Guangxue Society, the YMCA Advancement Association, the Siming Middle School, the Yongjiang Girls' Middle School, and the Dahua Magazine Company, as well as a supervisor of the Shanghai Trust Company. Mr. Wu has been serving society for nearly ten years. He has profound knowledge of both Chinese and Western cultures and is proficient in all six laws. He now wishes to use his many years of experience in serving society, protecting human rights, and promoting the rule of law. We cannot help but congratulate the judicial circles of our country.

The first edition of He's painting album was printed in 500 copies and sold out in less than half a year, which shows how deeply He's art moves people and how much he is believed. Now the second edition of He's painting album, printed in 500 copies, will be published soon to meet the needs of society. The book has a total of seventeen pages, one foot and three inches long, and is printed in collotype, which is clearer than the first edition. The original price is three yuan per copy, but during the re-edition period, the special price is one yuan and a half, plus postage of one jiao and three fen. It is sold at He Lu, 17 Xihu Lane, Ximen Road, Shanghai.

Variety Literature Special Issue Published - The Variety Literature Memorial Lu Xun Death Anniversary Special Issue will be published today, still published by Variety Literature Publishing House, edited by Yu Qiufan. The issue contains a large portrait of Lu Xun's remains, finely printed in color, for those who admire Mr. Lu to hang. There are also specially written mourning articles by Zhang Naiqi, Dong Qiufang, Hu Xingzhi, Yu Qiufan, etc. In addition, there are also novels and poems written by other writers, totaling more than one hundred and twenty pages, which is more than before. The price is 20 cents, still distributed by Shanghai Magazine Company. It is now heard that the publishing house has prepared special discount coupons to give preferential treatment to new subscribers. Those who hold the coupon can subscribe to the magazine for half a year for only one yuan and for the whole year for only one yuan and six jiao, including postage, directly from the publishing house at 148 Avenue Joffre.

Mass (Cartoon, Film, Literature) Bi-monthly Published Today - The Mass Magazine at 373 Bazilu Road, Shanghai, combines cartoons, films, and literature into a popular bi-monthly, published today. The content is rich, exquisite, and novel. Cartoons: more than one hundred masterpieces by Hu Kao, Lu Zhixiang, Zhang Leping, Huang Yaoshan, etc. Films: more than five thousand words and more than twenty copperplate illustrations by Yang Cunxu, Zhao Da, Fan, etc. Literature: five thousand words of creations by Xu Xu, Hei Ying, Bai Cun, Ji Ren, etc. The three are combined into one volume, and the price is only one jiao. The annual subscription is two yuan and four jiao.

Zhejiang Literature Exhibition Special Issue

Preface

— Xu Shaodi

Since the Tang and Song dynasties, Zhejiang has long been a land of culture and relics. In the history of Chinese culture, both Zhejiang provinces have had unlimited glory. In recent years, while Zhejiang's construction projects have been progressing rapidly, the education community has not dared to slack off. Despite difficult material conditions, it has strived for various improvements and has achieved some results. It has always been believed that the education cause has a wide range of objects and many aspects. In school education, in the history, geography, and civics subjects, we should pay attention to the lectures on the deeds of the sages of our hometowns to arouse their admiration and inspiration. To broaden and deepen its effectiveness, we should especially use the methods of social education so that the general public can feel its influence. This is the meaning of the exhibition.

In 1934, Zhejiang Province held a provincial conditions exhibition, which was rich in the meaning of local education. However, the scope of the exhibition was wider, and the collection of literature of the sages of this province was rare. In recent years, the Education Department has always been responsible for praising the humanistic aspects of the previous generations to the local libraries and folk education centers, and in 1935, it was included in the plan to hold a Zhejiang Literature Exhibition. The Provincial Library has been collecting new and old books and has been paying attention to the collection and collation of literature from this province. Therefore, it was assigned to the library to host the event, which began on October 1st of this year after a period of preparation. During the solicitation, collection branches were set up in various special districts of the province and in Beijing, Ping, and Shanghai, and the heads of the counties were ordered by the Education Department to engage in the collection, and exhibitions were held in each county or district before selecting the best to send to the province. The power of the group inside and outside the province was gathered, and a large number of writings, calligraphy, portraits, rubbings, and cultural relics of the local sages were collected, which is a matter of deep consolation.

The purpose of the exhibition is to elaborate on the literature of Zhejiang Province and promote artistic education. However, what I want to say to the people of the province and the visiting guests is that when we look at the various cultural relics on display, we can see the essence of the ancient carved editions, but what we should pay attention to is definitely not only this form. We should think of the people from the objects, and know how the sages of Zhejiang diligently studied and practiced, how they were loyal to the country, and how they connected their lives with the safety and survival of the nation, and did not hesitate to give up their lives and property for the country. This great and magnificent spirit of the local sages should be deeply understood, carried forward, and promoted by us. The feeling of love for the hometown is aroused, and the spirit of the nation is inspired by the love for the hometown, and it is dedicated to our troubled country. The exhibition will not be criticized for playing with things and losing ambition and being infatuated with the past, but it can exert its profound educational significance. The exhibition will be edited and published in the daily newspaper, so I will write down my feelings at the beginning.

The Purpose of the Zhejiang Literature Exhibition

— Chen Xunci

Since the opening of the sea, the customs have gradually changed. Zhejiang, a land of cultural relics, has contributed to today's academic undertakings in many ways, but the industry of praising and examining the humanities of the previous generations is gradually being abandoned. Therefore, the study and research of ancient classics is gradually becoming rare, and those who know the literature sigh. The Zhejiang Provincial Library inherits the old traditions of Wenlan, gathers the classics of the new and the old, and always tries its best to preserve and promote the literature of the province. This time, under the command of the Education Department, the Zhejiang Literature Exhibition is held, relying on the help of all walks of life inside and outside the province, and the collection of exhibits has been quite complete. At the beginning of the exhibition, I would like to state the four meanings of the meeting in order to clarify the purpose of the meeting, and also to discuss with the sages at home and abroad.

First, collect and preserve the writings of local scholars. The scholars of Zhejiang have written as many books as there are trees in the forest. The Siku Quanshu records 1,390 authors, 743 books, and a total of 2,268 books. The number of books that were lost by the Siku and those that were written after Qianlong and were not included is undoubtedly countless. How much more are there that have not been published, or have been printed but are rarely passed down? Nowadays, private collections are declining, and libraries want to collect and visit but are short of funds. This exhibition collects the collections of more than 70 counties in Zhejiang Province and collectors inside and outside the province. Not only can the original manuscripts of famous authors be compared, but the scholars of the rocks and the cloth will also have the effect of elucidating the mysteries and expressing the micro by this collection. After the meeting, the objects will be returned to their original owners. Even if the Zhejiang Library is unable to make copies of the most isolated copies, it will be enough to provide scholars with information and pass on the essence of the former philosophers.

Second, promote the academic style of Zhejiang. The development of culture in Zhejiang has benefited from the migration of the nation to the south in the Jin and Song dynasties. Therefore, the scholarship has also been flourishing since the Southern Song Dynasty. Since then, the sectarian styles have been passed down, and the local habits have been nurtured. It has gradually established its own special academic style. Such as being broad and able to keep the agreement, tolerant and not establishing portals, diligently studying and not neglecting practice, managing the world and focusing on practical use, in the scholars of Zhejiang in recent centuries, there is often a common spirit to be found. And in the study of classics, philosophy, literature, and even the study of xiangjiao, Zhejiang has had leaders in all generations, forming a flourishing trend of dividing ways and advancing together. As shown in this exhibition, it is even more possible to see the beauty of the academic style of Zhejiang throughout the ages. Unfortunately, since the world has become more urgent, scholars have tended to seek immediate results, and the fashion of practicing in seclusion has gradually declined. The decline of Zhejiang learning is fearful. How can we elucidate the excellent academic style of our sages of the past generations and inherit and carry it forward? It is the common goal of Zhejiang people to strive for. Moreover, Zhejiang people have always had no sense of closure, and the teachings of masters and famous Confucian scholars have often been widely spread to other places. Examining the way of cultivating oneself and others, how can Zhejiang people revive their academic style, and how can our countrymen jointly draw on the good style of Zhejiang and further purify it, and change the trend of the whole country to a healthy state, which should be the important mission of this meeting.

Third, sort out the local literature. The idea of respecting and congratulating the mulberry and zither and engaging in the collection and promotion of local literature has been well-known in Zhejiang for a long time. Song Confucian Wang Shenning's Siming Literature Collection can be a prominent example. After the middle of the Qing Dynasty, the style of compiling and publishing the works of the local sages as a series was also unique to Zhejiang Province. Successive people have continued to this day. (The Taizhou Series was the first, and in recent years there have been the Xianju Series, the Chuzhou Series, and the Siming Series, which is even more grandiose in scale and is being continued.) Looking back on the past, the superiors were not as diligent in advocating as the sages of the past. The private property of the individual is less than that of the ancient times. Therefore, the writings of the sages are gradually lost, and the ancient monuments and scenic spots are also lacking in sorting. Even the general history of a province has been missing for two hundred years; the compilation of the epigraphy has not been heard to have continued the tradition of Ruan Wenda. We can see from the inscriptions on the cultural relics on display in this exhibition that the literature of a place is easily lost. Therefore, all the work of literature collation, such as the repair of ancestral halls and tombs, the preservation of epigraphy, and even the re-editing of the county chronicles and provincial chronicles, and the preservation of Pingzhi materials, should be done by the standing bureaus of the provinces and counties and the people of the local area with a heart. The province will take the lead in the area, even in today's world of honoring shame and cultivating martial arts, it is believed that the construction of the Confucius Temple, the creation of the Stele Forest, and the planning and construction of the general history are all closely related to the importance of political education, and should be planned early and not delayed.

Fourth, promote the spirit of patriotism and love for the country. Loving the hometown and loving the country are the same source, and they are related to each other, and there is no prejudice. The people of Zhejiang are sincere in their hometowns, and the humanities of Zhejiang are the most closely related to the safety and survival of the nation. Tracing back to ancient times, Gou Jian's determination to rejuvenate the country was the first to establish a model. Later, the Eastern Jin Dynasty was in a state of partial security, and the two Xie used a battle to protect the overall situation; the capital of Lin'an was settled, and Zong Zhongjian (Ze) used the garrison to resist the enemy's atmosphere. In the Ming Dynasty, there were Song Lian and Liu (Ji) who assisted in the creation of the emperor's career, and Yu Zhongsu who stabilized the country. During the Ming Dynasty, the loyal and martyrs of Zhejiang rose up, Ningbo Qian Zhongjie (Sule), Zhang Cangshui (Huangyan), and Dongyang Zhang Yusi (Guowei) were the most prominent. In the Qing Dynasty's revolutionary campaign, Ke Fengfu made great contributions, and many of the elites of Zhejiang gave their lives to achieve benevolence, or assisted in their success with words. This exhibition, Zhou Yuan Zizhu, Jiangguan solicited, and paid special attention to the literature related to the expression of the past philosophers and the guidance of the people's spirit; all the martyrs of the revolution and the sages of Zhejiang who have contributed to the nation have tried their best to seek their portraits, writings, and objects. The purpose of the exhibition is not only to promote the figures of a province, but also to show this great and magnificent atmosphere, so that the people of Zhejiang and even the patriots of the whole country will rise up when they hear the news. It is good that the national fortune is difficult at this time, and foreign insults are very difficult. This spirit of loving the hometown and defending the country should be possessed by the people of the country. We hope that the viewers will examine it carefully and deeply in order to achieve the effect of learning from the past and planning for the future, and not just be fascinated by the past with the scattered vermilion and ink, and avoid being criticized for playing with things and losing ambition.

Generally speaking, the exhibitions in our country in modern times are nothing more than three types: or they list cultural relics to examine academic studies; or they seek out products to encourage practical industries; or they only display calligraphy and paintings for people to appreciate. The famous cities and large cities in the south, in order to meet the needs of the times, attach great importance to the second, while Hangzhou is more beautiful and respects literature, and there are more calligraphy and painting exhibitions. As for the cultural relics exhibitions with academic significance, the old capital has always been regarded as the most prominent. This exhibition of the Zhejiang Museum intends to promote the academic style in addition to elaborating on the literature of Zhejiang Province. Even if it fails to achieve the effect of changing the atmosphere, it also wants to try its initial scaffold for a wider cultural relic exhibition. During the solicitation, collection branches were set up in the nine special areas of the province and in Nanjing, Beiping, and Shanghai. There were also local sages who were kind and good to me and lent many treasures. The main points were that the productions of Zhejiang people or those related to Zhejiang were returned. The special heads and county heads of the provinces, the local elders, and the academic institutions and scholars outside the province provided various kinds of assistance, which is deeply appreciated. If this meeting can be roughly impressive and slightly effective, it is all thanks to the protection of the public. As for the improper display and the mistakes in the examination and compilation, the colleagues of the Zhejiang Museum should apologize to the visitors and ask for their correction. (Written on October 28, 1936 at the Zhejiang Library)

The Relationship between Zhejiang Literature and Modern China

— Liu Yizheng

In modern China, the literature of Zhejiang has the greatest relationship. The Mongolians were barren and the Ming Dynasty rose up. Although the Zhu family started in Haosi, they planned brightly and created the Xia Dynasty. The strength of the public officials of Yiwu, Jinhua, and Qingtian also contributed. The learning system of Min declined after its peak. Yangming changed its banner and became the patriarch of a generation. Lishan and Lizhou did not replace it, and the flow spread to the neighboring areas. The light and spirit of Zhejiang to China and Asia is so great. The Manchu Qing painfully eradicated the Zhejiang scholars, and the Zhejiang scholars huddled in the lewd power. The literary writings increasingly portrayed their spirituality, and the thoughts of the bereaved people for the country and the nation were hidden. The knives and saws killed people, and the feathers and benefits could not destroy and corrupt them. Shanyin and Yuhang, ordinary people, were able to take advantage of Changbai's disadvantages and donate their lives to overturn their tripods. The extreme of Yunhui caused a turmoil for 20 years. From the broken mountains and rivers, they held the literature, industry, party rule, and military power, and ran around to control the world. Only the heroes of Zhejiang did it. Alas, the people of Zhejiang have shouldered China for five or six hundred years, and what is expressed by the side of Zhejiang's literature is also the Taoist. The difficult times are coming, and the chariots are coming. I hope that those who view this meeting will hold my words as needles and fruits, and expand the ambitions of the former philosophers. With my China and Asia, the influence of this meeting is not only limited to one province and one place.

It is too late to plan to attach the special issue of the Literature Exhibition to the Daily News, and the solicitation of articles is allowed to be hasty. Mr. Liu Yimou of Dantu replied that because the time was short, he did not write a special article, but answered his request with a title. In order to facilitate the readers, he proposed a title based on the meaning of the text. I hope Mr. Liu and the readers will understand.

Essential Description of Precious Items in the Zhejiang Literature Exhibition

— Cha Ke

Although the Zhejiang Province's Literature Exhibition has been affected by the current situation, thanks to the enthusiastic support of public and private collectors from various regions, the exhibition is filled with a dazzling array of precious items. Unfortunately, due to the hurried timeframe, the arrival of items from different locations varied, and the procedures for inspection, registration, review, and classification were extremely cumbersome, preventing the compilation of a complete catalog for visitors. Here, we will briefly introduce some of the notable items that have been recorded, providing a glimpse of the collection.

The scope of the collection covers both the north and south, with the majority of submissions coming from within the province. As of October 26th, over 20,000 items, comprising more than 6,000 different types, have been received, with over half having been selected. Among them, noteworthy items include: (1) Manuscripts of local worthies, such as Ming Dynasty Shanyin resident Zhang Dai's manuscript "Stone Cabinet Book" (believed to have been plagiarized by Gu Yingtai) and "Tao'an Manuscripts"; Chen Hongshou of Zhuji's handwritten first draft of "Lun Tang Collection"; Wu Yanku'ang of Yongjia's "Flower History"; Wang Yizhong of Qingtian's "Record of Suppressing Bandits"; and manuscripts such as Qi Zhaonan of Tiantai's "Yuzhi Hall Collection of Writings", Sun Yirang of Rui'an's "Original Manuscripts of Names and Origins," Huang Yizhou of Dinghai's "Original Manuscripts of Jing Ji Miscellaneous Works," and Zhang Binglin of Yu Hang's "Qu Shu" manuscript. (2) Collated Editions, such as Qian Taiji of Jiaxing's hand-copied and collated "Laozi's Daodejing," and Sun Yirang of Rui'an's collated "General Explanation of Rites." (3) Manuscript Copies, such as Xu Wei's handwritten collection of essays and Cha Chubo's handwritten poems from the Ming and Qing dynasties, respectively, are considered treasures of the book world. (4) There are many rare portraits of local worthies, including an image of Qian Wusu Wang of Wuyue, a painting of Yang Ci Hu from the Song Dynasty (painted in the late Ming), a painting of Liu Wencheng Giving Lessons for Generations (painted by Chen Laolian), a portrait of seven generations of Wang Wencheng Gong, a portrait of Fan Dongming (Qin), portraits of Mao Xihe and Quan Xieshan from the Qing Dynasty, and a portrait of Xihe and Zhu Zhuzhai (painted by Ding Xiaoya with inscriptions by Ji Yun, Cheng Jin, Qian Daxin, etc.), and portraits of Zhang Cangshui and Qian Zhongjie. There are also numerous large photographs of other portraits, numbering in the hundreds. (5) Relics of local worthies are the most difficult to collect, due to the lack of attention given to them by the Chinese people and the high regard shown by collectors. However, items collected include Qian Wusu Wang's Tian Ce Tang precious jade seal, Yuan Dynasty Plum Blossom Taoist Wu Zhonggui's inkstone, Wang Huaibin's court tablet from Yunhe in the Ming Dynasty, Zheng Xiao's iron helmet used during the defense against Japanese pirates in Haiyan, Zhang Cangshui's inkstone (collected by the Yang family of Cixi, very precious), Leqing Heshan Renbai's inkstone, Chen Guifen of Tiantai's champion armor from the Qing Dynasty, and Zhang Shuwei's inscription on Qin measuring devices from Jiaxing. Among them, relics of revolutionary martyrs, along with their writings, are displayed in a separate section dedicated to (6) National Revolution Literature (limited to people from Zhejiang). Due to the difficulty of collecting these items, the collection is limited. However, items such as the Guangfuhui history written in pencil by Tao Huanqing, leader of the Guangfuhui, three days before his martyrdom, Ao Mengjiang of Jiaxing's secret propaganda material "Ancestor Worship and Blessing Book" and prayers, and Xu Bosun of Shanyin's early drawing of the Chinese coastal map, are rarely seen by the Chinese people. These are unlike the writings of Qiu Jin and portraits of martyrs from Shanyin, which have been exhibited in the province before. Chen Yingshi's blood-stained clothes, cherished by the Lake Society, are rarely displayed to the public. This time, through the efforts of the association, it was possible to bring them for public viewing, complementing the bronze statue on the lake. (7) The selected collection of over 500 scrolls of calligraphy and paintings by local worthies is exceptionally beautiful. Notable works include Wu Zhen's imitation of Mi Fu's landscape painting from the Yuan Dynasty, Ren Daoxun of Rui'an's hanging scroll of landscape painting from the Ming Dynasty, Chen Laolian's "Reading in the Creek and Mountain" painting, Mao Xihe's vertical scroll of "Jade Long Stone", and Dai Wenjie Gong's bamboo painting from Qiantang. Countless other masterpieces are also on display. A book by Xia Gui of Song Dynasty Qiantang is included, but its authenticity is questionable. As for Yue Zhongwu's authentic writing and Ge Xiaoxian's handwritten letter from Linhai, they are not yet counted among the works of ten thousand worthies. Other (8) printed books include the "Ksitigarbha Dharani Sutra" printed during the Later Zhou dynasty, discovered at Tianning Temple in Huzhou (20 years earlier than the scripture rolls from the Leifeng Pagoda), Song Dynasty supervised editions, Chen Jie Yuan's bookshop editions, Yuan Dynasty West Lake Academy editions, and fine prints from Zhejiang during the Ming and Qing dynasties, providing a view of the history of printing in Zhejiang. (9) Collections of books, including editions from Fan's Tianyige, Qi's Danshengtang from the Ming Dynasty, Zhu's Qiancaitang, Bao's Zhibuzu Zhai from the Qing Dynasty, and Ding's Baqian Juan Lou, and Sun's Yuhai Lou, have been selected for display. Rare items include Yan Jiuneng's inscription on Zhou Yigong's manuscript from the Song Dynasty, and Wu Meicun's hand-copied "Collection of Mr. Zhou from Linpu" from Qiancaitang, which are considered treasures of the book world. (10) Election documents, including a large number of Ming and Qing provincial examination records, the Ming Dynasty examination lists from Ningbo Tianyige, and other important documents have been collected. The most eye-catching items include the original marked examination papers of Qi Chengcan and Qi Biaojia, father and son from Ming Dynasty Shanyin, and the silver cup used by Zhang Wei Chi of Xiaochu Haiyan from Zhang's Sheyuan at Ma Mingzhi's banquet (also listed as relics of local worthies), and the court attire and palace examination papers of Chen Shengqin from Qing Dynasty Tiantai. (11) Very few official documents have been collected, but items such as the memorial submitted by Grand Secretary Hu Zhaolong during the Shunzhi period of the Qing Dynasty, accusing Zhang Dajie of bribing Jinshi Shen of Huzhou, and the report by Zhejiang Governor Ruan Yuan in the 14th year of Jiaqing, as well as the final draft of the Yang Naiwu case preserved by Yu Hang County, are valuable. (12) The collection of Zhejiang local chronicles is very rich, including Song Dynasty editions of Siming Zhi and Chicheng Zhi, as well as Ming and Qing Dynasty chronicles. In addition to the items collected by the Zhejiang Library over the past 30 years, treasures from Tianyige, Jiaye Lou, Jiufeng's old collection, the Peking Library, Jinling University, and other private collections have been brought together, creating a grand spectacle. (13) The charts include forty new Zhejiang historical and geographical maps, as well as old Zhejiang maps from the Ming and Qing dynasties borrowed from the Huaping Library, which are well-prepared. Various economic and transportation maps sent by construction organizations are not included. (14) The genealogy section includes genealogies from prominent families in various regions of the province during the Ming and Qing dynasties. The Zhejiang Library already had a collection, and local borrowing has added to the display. Among them, the Song Dynasty genealogy treasured by the Chen family of Fengqiao, Zhuji, is considered particularly valuable. The beginning of the genealogy includes Emperor Gaozong's inscription from the 15th year of Shaoxing, portraits of Chen Shengbi, Chen Yaozu, Yaozi, and others, and the "Seal of the Imperial Song Dynasty." It is said that there are many old genealogies from the Song and Yuan dynasties that have been passed down, but this is the only one that has been generously loaned to the association for display, making it a rare and difficult to see masterpiece. (15) There are very few original gold and stone artifacts on display, but the Wu Yue gold-plated pagoda and Tang Dynasty stone scripture pillar are quite precious. The rubbings, including those collected by the Zhejiang Library over the years and those sent from various parties, are numerous. Among them, in addition to Yitaku rubbings, there are also old items from the Tang and Song dynasties. (16) There are not many steles and inscriptions on display, but there is a Dongyang version of the Lanting Collection. The Luoshen Fu written by Wang Youjun and rubbed on Southern Tang Chenxintang paper, provided by Mr. Sun Shefu, was once owned by the Qing Imperial Court, and the Zhu Zhang spots can be traced. Although it does not have a special connection with Zhejiang literature, it is a treasure of this art form. The collection of cultural relics is vast, and the arrangement of the manuscripts is not yet complete. This hasty compilation may contain omissions and inaccuracies. We hope to provide a detailed account after further investigation in the future. (Editor's note: The catalog and inscriptions of this exhibition will be published in the "Wenlan Journal" Volume 2, Issues 2 and 4, a special exhibition edition published by the Zhejiang Library.)

Editor's Notice

For the special issue of the Zhejiang Literature Exhibition, the Zhejiang Library sent letters in advance to solicit contributions or poems and inscriptions from scholars inside and outside the province. We are deeply grateful for the generous contributions from various sectors. However, due to the limited space available for special issues in various newspapers, in addition to those published in the Shen Bao (Day 1), Southeast Daily (Day 2), Ta Kung Pao (Day 3), and Zheng Bao (Day 1, separately), (most of which are not repeated, please pay attention), many others could not be published due to space constraints. For example, Mr. Zhu Shijia's "Study of the Three Records of Lin'an," Mr. Qian Baozong's "Record of Zhejiang Astronomers," Mr. Jiang Fucong's "Study of Seals of Zhejiang Book Collectors," Mr. Qian Nanyang's "Drama of Zhejiang," and Mr. Chen Yiyang's "Study of the Qian Family's Iron Certificate" could not be published due to their length and the small size of the newspaper. At the beginning of the solicitation, it was stated that a special issue would be published in the "Wenlan Journal," and all the articles are in-depth studies and will be published in the "Wenlan Journal." The "Guofeng Monthly" also plans to publish a special issue on Zhejiang literature, and some articles may also be included in that publication for broader readership. We hope that the authors will understand.

Reading Club

Letter to Readers

— Shi Ying

Preface to "Stories of National Crisis"

My dear readers:

I often want to understand this: Why has our country reached this state? The danger of extinction is already before our eyes, some of our brothers have already become slaves of others, and some are about to be chained. Is it really as our elders and teachers say, that we Chinese are destined to suffer? I do not believe it. I searched for books and read many history books; these books have various different records. They tell me that our country once had glorious times, and had many things to be proud of. But since the big foreign bosses came to China to do business, they called China worse than each day. The national power of China has fallen from strong to its current state of decline in less than a hundred years. - These records in the books finally satisfied me. But I spent a long time searching for these things, reading several feet thick of books; I think that every Chinese person now has a question like mine, and must understand this, but not everyone has the time to do it like I do. I want to tell what I know, so that everyone knows. But my writing is very poor, I can't be like the gentlemen who wear square hats, doing it originally and deeply like lecture notes in university; or write exciting and impassioned articles with beautiful words. Fortunately, my readers are always afraid of headaches when reading lecture notes in school, and are afraid that exciting and impassioned articles are too empty and they get nothing. Let me write it in the most common words, like an old man in the countryside. I will not say any professional terms, I am not afraid of someone saying my things are crude and not like articles. I just write according to my meaning, and do my best to write clearly and understandably, so that readers can read on.

I am reluctant to mention many trivial names in my book. The reason why these people are able to leave their names in history is mostly not their own fault. What we need to know is all of us, our country, why we have come to this point. As for the big men, we don’t have to memorize their names; most of them rarely do us any good except for planning for themselves. My readers only need to know a few names, and that's enough. As for place names and other specialized terms in the book, I also use as few as possible, so as not to bother readers with these words. Therefore, my book is even less like a lecture in school. But after reading my book, if you can understand the situation of China being oppressed by the great powers in the past hundred years, then my goal will be achieved.

The name of my book is Stories of National Crisis. At first I wanted to use the name "Stories of the Oppression of China by the Great Powers in the Past Hundred Years", but what is very problematic is the three words "past hundred years". History is not a "magic lantern", watching one picture after another; history is a very long river, flowing from its source to the ocean, completely a long one, and cannot be divided into sections. The river water and sea water pass by wave after wave, and history also has the past, then the present, and the future. It is impossible to specify that on what year, what month, and what day, ancient times suddenly became modern times, and everything in the world was replaced. The stories I wrote in this book started from the Opium War; it is not to say that in 1840, the British suddenly had a whim to come to China to find fun, and then the Opium War broke out. Many past reasons have already determined the occurrence of the Opium War. But I have no choice; in order to save many trivial words, I had to cut the Gordian knot, abandon the past and not talk about it, and start by saying the Opium War. Because the current situation in China is completely caused by the events of the past sixty or seventy years, this book specifically explains the first few things in more detail; recent events, readers have heard and seen, and probably have some impressions left in their minds, so I will explain them more simply. However, I am not a tape recorder; it is not enough to simply report some news from the newspaper, what I talk about is naturally more systematic.

I am not a historian, and I don't have many books on hand, so mistakes in this book are inevitable; but I already want to thank my friends, they lent me valuable books to consult; I am not a writer, my book cannot be written vividly, so that readers feel as if they have personally experienced it, that is certain. Jun Lian was the first person to read this book. She has not attended a deep school, and she knows less about everything academic than I do. I had her read what I had written first, to see if she could understand everything. If she can't understand, then this passage has been tainted with a bit of civility, and I have to change it. I always go in the direction of being the easiest to understand.

I am waiting for readers to criticize after reading, and I hope my readers are willing to tell me. Finally, I would also like to thank the gentlemen in the Editorial and Translation Department of Kaiming Bookstore, because they gave me a lot of valuable instructions.

Further Explanation for Sha Meijun's Review of the Junior High School Singing Textbook

— Wu Mengfei

A book review cut from the Shanghai "Li Bao" on October 26th was forwarded by a friend, commenting on the "Junior High School Singing Textbook" that I edited. In addition to expressing gratitude to the reviewer, Sha Meijun, the editor really has a few words to declare:

The original review said: "Among them, except for the "Man Jiang Hong", "Youth Life", and "Tian Feng" songs, the rest are foreign tunes filled with Chinese words." In fact, "Tian Feng" is also a foreign tune, and the reviewer does not know its source. As for "Youth Life", although it is a domestic melody, the lyrics have been changed by the editor.

The original review also said: "Translating the lyrics of foreign songs into Chinese does not lose the original tune's mood. However, filling foreign tunes with Chinese words at will, regardless of whether they are suitable or not, as long as the number of words in the Chinese words can fit into the tune, is simply unreasonable." The editor also deeply sympathizes with this view, but it cannot be generalized. I often see that many of the foreign lyrics translated directly by the general public cannot be integrated with the original tune; and generally, the hymns sung by churches that are translated from foreign lyrics into Chinese are even grammatically incorrect, not to mention the rhyme. Does the reviewer think that such songs do not lose their original mood? As for taking foreign tunes and filling them with lyrics at will, it is certainly not feasible, but if you can match lyrics that are mutually integrated, it is not necessarily undesirable, and there is no need to match lyrics that praise something just because the original tune praises God. Originally. The expression of vocal music often relies on the meaning of the lyrics, and if the lyrics are erased, the listener can only feel a vague mood, so composers often mark the beginning of the song with words that indicate various musical interests, such as majestic, beautiful, cheerful, sad, etc. (all using professional musical terms). The person filling in the lyrics only needs to determine the rhythm of the original tune and not go against the meaning of the whole song. If, in addition to taking care of the mood of the song, it is necessary to seek complete identity in the meaning of the words, and then think that they are as unrelated as horses and oxen, I am afraid it is too rigid and outdated.

The three songs listed by the reviewer, "Missing Hometown", "Fearless Spirit", and "Abolish Unequal Treaties", were all selected by the editor from other publications, so the names of the composers and lyricists are marked on each song to clarify responsibility. Didn't the reviewer see this? However, the reason why the editor chose these three songs is of course because he thought that the three songs were generally still usable - except for a small part of the lyrics that are slightly criticizeable. The mood of "Missing Hometown" is expressive (Expressivo), the mood of "Fearless Spirit" tends to be beautiful, and the mood of "Abolish Unequal Treaties" is brave, which can generally be consistent with the Chinese lyrics. Does Sha Meijun think that if the original tune is about love, the filled lyrics must also be about love to match the mood? Then: I want to ask you to look up the foreign-published "Songs the Whole World Sings", which selects two original tunes for "Fearless Spirit": one is titled Believe me if all those Ende-aring Young Charms, and the other is titled Fair Harvard. It can be seen that foreigners are also using one tune for two purposes? Also, the original tune of "Abolish Unequal Treaties" is of course from Wagner's opera, but foreigners also match it with Flag of the free lyrics and sing it! (See foreign-published books such as "Songs the Children Love to Sing"). Will the reviewer laugh so hard that he can't close his mouth when he sees foreigners match the "Wedding March" with the lyrics of "Flag of Freedom"?

All in all: Our country's current music teaching materials are very poor. Ideally, it is best to create some songs with very appropriate and inseparable words and tunes. The editor is also trying and has already published them separately; as for using foreign tunes to fill in Chinese lyrics, it is a measure of expediency when one's own creation may not necessarily be better than the works of foreign musicians. Has the reviewer seen the "Collection of Music Teaching Materials for Middle Schools" and the "Collection of Music Teaching Materials for Elementary Schools" compiled by our Ministry of Education? Among them, a lot of time and procedures were spent collecting songs from all parts of the country, but the result is that most of them are foreign tunes filled with Chinese lyrics. Although my "Junior High School Singing Textbook" does not dare to claim to be a perfect work, it strives to avoid songs that are about spring flowers and autumn moons, and love and pity, and have no moaning, and there is absolutely no feeling of decadence and sadness, which is gratifying. It is difficult to be an editor, and it is not easy to review books. What does Sha Meijun think?

Needle for Youth Cultivation

— Zheng

"Continuation of Love's Education" - by Edmondo De Amicis - Translated by Xia Mianzun

Published by Kaiming Bookstore - Six Corners

I remember when I first left middle school and went to work as a trainee in a factory, I always felt dissatisfied with the work at hand. I either thought it was too mechanical or felt it was dull and tedious. At that time, I had read a few books bought from the market about professional self-cultivation, but most of what they talked about were grand principles such as "Suffering hardship is the price of success." On the one hand, I felt that I had not suffered "hardship," so of course, I didn't want to aspire to be "superior." On the other hand, I had always suspected that these old sayings were the idle talk of people who had already climbed to the top, and I was unwilling to accept them. It wasn't until later that I accidentally bought this book, "Continuation of Love's Education," and after its faithful and sincere explanation, it suddenly opened up my previous mood, and a bright and ideal path of life was clearly displayed before my eyes. I began to have hope, aspiration, and joy. Those monotonous tasks not only no longer bored me, but I also had great purpose in them.

How could this book have such great power? Because it can tell us, in a kind and thorough explanation, the attitude we should have towards "being a person;" it makes us know how to deal with the environment around us, and how to extract rich knowledge and proper fun from the things we encounter and hear every day. The old saying "Suffering hardship is the price of success" often makes us feel bitter even about things that are not bitter, but this book clearly tells us that there is no "bitter" word to be found in any legitimate career, just as there is no "difficult" word to be found in Napoleon's dictionary.

This book is written entirely in the style of a novel. It begins by saying that Enrico, the protagonist of "Love's Education," became seriously ill after entering middle school because he worked too hard. After recovering from his illness, he was sent by his parents to his uncle's house by the sea to recuperate. The uncle is an old man with gray hair, strong and gentle, like a "kind lion." He has pure but not extravagant hopes for Enrico and wants to educate him into a healthy Italian citizen with sea-like passion. Most of the book is the old man's "sea beast's roar" like teachings, and the other part is his actions in a few months and Enrico's being influenced, as well as a few moving stories worth remembering.

Now, let's first take a look at what kind of person the uncle in the book is:

The uncle's chest is full of rich knowledge, but his knowledge is different from others. Other people's knowledge comes from books, but he "never received any education from anyone since he was a child, but used his own eyes to see and his own heart to think." He said, "There is a world that school teachers and school textbooks cannot teach. You must learn about this world yourself." "Studying the vast nature and living world is more important than schoolwork." "No matter what corner of nature, or who you meet on the road, can become your living knowledge... Nature is the mother of wisdom, the teacher's teacher." He lost his father at the age of ten, dropped out of school, and went to live a life at sea; later, he became a captain, but what is most gratifying is that he actually learned a sea-like great personality and sea-like rich knowledge. Why did he have such success? Please see the precious teachings of a pastor to him:

"Don't be discouraged. Even if you are a sailor, you can still hope to become a captain. As long as you have ambition, you can become any famous person... No occupation is shameful..."

"Starting tomorrow, please swear every morning that you must do three good things in a day. When you go to bed at night, please reflect on whether you have actually done the three good things you planned to do today. If you do this, your life will not be wasted for a day. As long as you can do this, you don't need to go to school anymore, and you don't need to wait for the teacher's teaching." How did he implement these teachings?

"...He works hard every day: first, to improve his health, second, to improve his heart, and third, to cultivate his thoughts. He does this until he is old, without interruption.

His personality cultivation is indeed the greatest success in his life:

First, although his appearance is like a barbarian, his heart is full of correct "love." He not only loves his friends and relatives in his memory, loves his country, but also loves all people universally. For the sake of love, sometimes he is very strict, sometimes he becomes very gentle, and sometimes he is very brave. When we read "Dog and Man," about his rescue of the child who was bitten by a dog, everyone cannot help but respect him! When we read "Pork Buns and Tragic Memories," about how he used straightforward friendship to transform a treacherous Brospi into such a tame person, everyone cannot help but shed a few tears of joy! His love is sometimes not only applied to human beings but also to plants and trees. This is easily seen in "Plants and Trees That Understand Words." He said, "Trees, like me, can feel, can be happy, can endure, and, alas! They, like me, will also die!" How kind these words are!

Second, his artistic cultivation is very profound. He likes the fierce ocean, and he also likes the earth, the mother of life. His heart is full of beautiful poems. He once said, "People should all be poets. People rely on hope, some become farmers, some become fishermen, some become factory workers, some become sailors, and some become mechanics. But no matter what occupation they are engaged in, if their hearts are not the hearts of poets, they cannot bloom beautiful flowers of life." But what is the poetry he is talking about? It is not empty praise, nor is it gratuitous sadness. It is the crystallization of hot blood and soul, the smile of struggle and victory. He believes that the light of Italy is all a gift from the great poet Dante. Therefore, he believes that poetry can save the country, as long as it is done in this way: "Don't be discouraged in everything, hold hope, and move forward actively and bravely. If you encounter difficulties, always regard them as a precursor to new victories and expect them in the future, and, in just things, you must be a hero. In order to show the spirit of beauty, you should not fear anything."

Third, he is upright, decisive, and full of responsibility. He does things without hesitation, is generous, organized, and has insight. He helps the mad beggar but is not fooled by false philanthropists. When he lost the borrowed counterfeit gold coins in his childhood, he immediately used all the money in his pocket to buy real ones to compensate. He despises money and vanity. He is willing to help others with all his strength, but he does not want people to exchange for false gifts.

In such a thin book, this old great man has fully entrusted all these great cultivations that he has painstakingly pondered. What he wants to teach and influence is not only his nephew Enrico, but the entire Italian nation, not only the entire Italian nation, but all of humanity. His greatest contribution is to point out a bright path in life for us. He tells us that we should seek precious and beautiful poetry from places that are usually not noticed. As long as we bravely enjoy, work, appreciate, and think about these beautiful poems, a great power will be born from these poems, and this power will enable you to break through all obstacles without pain, like sea waves, like the wind, like lightning forward!

In many places, in addition to feeling the author's superb thoughts, we cannot help but admire the beauty of his writing style. According to the preface, the author was originally an Italian poet, which is very credible; because the text of the entire book is almost everywhere as light, beautiful, and majestic as poetry. Some of the descriptions cannot be written by ordinary novelists. Please see the following paragraphs:

The uncle's physique is strong, although not very slender, with broad shoulders, all gray hair, heavy beard, clear eyebrows, and with a slight frown, you can hardly see his eyes under the long eyebrows.

The uncle's eyes are really strange. The light like gazing at the angry tide and the soft light are always shining alternately.

The uncle is impatient and often gets angry, but once the thunder passes, it is over, and he is very gentle afterward.

The uncle's color is tanned like red copper. His face is engraved with deep, gully-like wrinkles. At first glance, he seems terrible. But on closer inspection, he is full of kindness in his strength, like an old, kind lion. —Page 10—

The child wore a sleeveless white flannel shirt, revealing a small head and shoulders like spring flowers from the thin gauze collar. Its atmosphere is so clear, pure, and clean, like the morning sun, almost making people imagine the dawn of a new era. —Page 74—

Finally, I, like the translator Mr. Xia Mianzun, "hope that tens of millions of young people in the country who are not fortunate enough to go to school can get a kind of comfort from this book and develop a kind of courageous self-confidence!"

Mill silk and other varieties had better sales, and the price was quite stable, it is said.

Needle-like and Eyebrow-like Green Tea Sold Slightly

Yesterday, in the foreign firm tea market, European firms' dealers had already filled the purchase orders made by foreign telegrams last week. Since Saturday was only a half-day market, the market situation became even more desolate. Only Xiehe Jinlong and other firms bought more than 200 boxes of needle-like, show eyebrow, and precious eyebrow green tea in the entire city.

According to a report from the Tea Warehouse Industry Association, after the green tea market started to move at the end of last week, the market situation developed immediately. This week, each foreign firm has been negotiating on each tea at market prices that are already in line with foreign prices. Transactions have been made for each tea. It is estimated that 1,850 boxes of precious eyebrow tea from all routes, 1,600 boxes of small needle-like eyebrow tea, 1,860 boxes of Pingshui pearl tea, 1,600 boxes of Gongxi tea from all routes, and about 1,000 boxes of Pingshui precious eyebrow tea were transacted. Other teas such as Phoenix eyebrow, shrimp eyebrow, and Pingshui No. 2 and 3 pearl tea also had hundreds of boxes transacted. It was found that the inventory of each tea has gradually decreased, and the market situation is also stable.

Piece Goods: After the Sharp Fall of Fourth Mill Estate Feather Yarn, etc., Low-Grade Goods from Our Factory Have All Retreated

Yesterday, the cloth market saw a slightly larger volume of Japanese-made fine cloth and fine twill transactions due to the handling of the month-end goods sample mortgage slip procedures. The volume of Chinese-made goods was very small. However, the amount of overdue futures that had not yet been settled for fine cloth, fine twill, straight tribute cloth, serge, broadcloth, floral velvet, and diagonal velvet, etc., was also huge, all of which had to be delivered upon arrival. The market was flat yesterday, and business in all sectors remained sluggish. The selling prices of various goods also uniformly declined. Fine cloth, fine twill, coarse cloth, and coarse twill fell by about a dime (per piece). In particular, the rebound of heavyweight coarse cloth was the most severe, with some mills falling by two dimes (per piece). About 200 pieces in total of 16-pound and 14-pound military uniforms were transacted. After the sharp fall of third mill estate goods, raw silk, etc., by about three dollars, low-grade goods from our factory, such as Xinhua Xinliao Tu, Gongsheng Pioneer Brand, Dafeng Caishen Brand, and Yuantong Da Deli Brand, all rebounded, falling by three to five dimes per piece. Printed straight tribute cloth and serge from various factories such as Hengfeng's internal and external factories, as well as straight tribute cloth, broadcloth, melton, and serge from various factories, all fell by about five li (per yard). However, most factories are still holding firm because they have undelivered orders and no inventory accumulation, so they are temporarily resisting loosening prices. Children's Special

Statistics: Tung Oil Trade in September – Limited Progress in European and American Markets, Stagnant Conditions in Shanghai and Hankou

According to the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, Shanghai's tung oil exports in September totaled 3,839 metric tons, a decrease of 2,777 metric tons compared to the 6,616 metric tons in the same month last year. The total for the first nine months of this year was 78,798 metric tons, a decrease of 27,822 metric tons compared to the 106,620 metric tons in the same period last year. Further investigation shows that Hankou's export volume this month totaled 28,623 metric tons, an increase of 7,779 metric tons compared to the same month last year. The total for the first nine months of this year was 353,460 metric tons, an increase of 89,856 metric tons compared to the same period last year. Domestic tung oil exports from Shanghai this month totaled 542 metric tons, an increase of 284 metric tons compared to the same month last year. The total for the first nine months of this year was 11,543 metric tons, an increase of 5,107 metric tons compared to the same period last year.

Regarding the tung oil market this month, with the arrival of new oil approaching, both buyers and sellers adopted a wait-and-see attitude. Inventories were still abundant, and supply was quite active. However, European and American demand remained sluggish, resulting in quiet transactions and a downward trend in the market. Although there were occasional transactions by foreign firms in Hankou, no large deals were made. At the beginning of the month, the market hovered around 61-62 yuan, but then consistently declined, even falling below 50 yuan by the 19th. Subsequently, the market became uncertain and fell into a state of stagnation. Although foreign firms had some spot goods to sell, their asking prices were too low, and traders were generally unwilling to sell, leading to an almost complete standstill in spot trading.

Shanghai oil prices softened due to frequent declines in Hankou. Foreign firms showed little interest, and the market atmosphere was quiet. Zhejiang oil was also affected by the decline in white tung oil and depreciated accordingly. General hoarders, anticipating the arrival of new oil, lowered prices to sell off their stocks. The chaos in the market in the early part of the last ten days of the month, when prices fell to 48 yuan, can be imagined.

Securities: Public Bond Trading Very Quiet

Yesterday, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange was extremely sluggish, with a slightly weakening trend. Trading by all parties was very slow. Due to the depressed situation and it being Saturday, various sectors were observing, and the number of attendees at the meeting was particularly scarce. Only the first session in the morning saw more transactions, and subsequent sessions were extremely quiet. Major players remained on the sidelines. Market sentiment remained stable, but it was anticipated that something unfavorable would inevitably happen in North China. Yesterday's trading saw scattered transactions at the opening, with prices falling by a few cents. The closing was quiet. Category B near-term and long-term bonds, and Category A near-term bonds, failed to open. Category E long-term and Category D near-term bonds showed no movement. The remaining bonds fluctuated slightly, with differences of only five cents. The afternoon opening saw most bonds unchanged, with a few rising or falling by five cents or a dime. However, Category A near-term bonds rose by 15 cents. The closing was even quieter, with only Category D and C long-term bonds showing a rise or fall of 10 cents. Most others remained unchanged, and a few did not open. The quiet situation was unprecedented. The final market prices showed only Category D near-term bonds rising by 10 cents, while the rest mostly fell by five cents to two dimes. The total transaction volume was 1.84 million yuan. The results of the price fluctuations are compared in the table below. (Unit: Yuan, Transaction Unit: 100 Yuan)
