More Hexia Rice Arriving Daily, Sales Still Slow… Market Prices Declining

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the supply from various regions became even more abundant, with 63 or 64 boats arriving, carrying a total of 13,500 to 13,600 shi (a unit of dry measure). Thin rice accounted for two-thirds of the total, and thin rice was selling well. Merchants from Qingdao, Yantai, and other regions bought 4,000 to 5,000 packages. However, the market conditions were still not good, because the supply was indeed abundant. Despite this buying activity, supply still exceeded demand, leaving a considerable surplus. This led to harsh demands from the buyers, while sellers were more discouraged. As a result, the price of green rice continued to decline, with high-quality rice depreciating by 25 cents and mid-grade rice depreciating by 20 cents. The reason why mid-grade rice depreciated slightly less than high-quality rice was that it had already fallen more in the previous market. Thick new japonica rice remained unchanged, only selling in rural areas. The price was slightly adjusted due to scarcity. Looking back at the overall situation, with the daily surge in shipments, it is still difficult to predict whether the buying activity will lead to a better market. The arrival and sales of Du Yang sharp-pointed rice were equal, with no rise or fall in price. Since Yin Yuan rice had been declining steadily for days, it is now showing a high-stable and medium-weak situation. There is no fixed standard for thick and thin broken japonica rice.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, 42 or 43 boats arrived from various Hexia routes. Sales of various goods in the market remained slow. The price of medium-grade new japonica rice fell by 7-8 cents, the price of Yang Du sharp-pointed rice fell by 5-6 cents, the price of Yin Yuan rice fell by 10-20 cents, and the price of top-grade thin rice also fell by about 10 cents. The price of Jiashan Baige rice fell by 20 cents. The sales of various sharp-pointed rice from other regions were not smooth, and prices were barely maintained. In the evening market, the price of a special new japonica rice called Yao Liangbao from Changzhou was sold for 10 yuan and 9 cents, which has not been seen since the Western New Year.

Guangdong Province Still the Main Destination for Ke Xian Rice

Yesterday, the arrival and sales of Ke Xian rice both decreased, and the market returned to a stable state. Yesterday, Ke Xian rice was still mainly sold to Guangdong merchants, with more than 5,200 packages sold throughout the day. Only 100 packages of Taiwan Xian rice were sold by this street, and the rest were all bought by Guangdong merchants. With local demand sluggish and little interest from northern merchants, the market could have declined. However, the continued demand from Guangdong kept people optimistic. A total of 2,134 packages of Jiangxi rice, 300 packages of Hunan rice, 3,080 packages of Shanghai Han brown rice, and 180 packages of Taiwan Xian rice were sold. Prices were similar to the previous day. Sellers wanted to raise prices, but were prevented by the weakening sales to Guangdong.

Children! If you want to save money, it is explained in detail there, I will not repeat it.

The Sailing of the Ship

—Zhen

One day, Min'er's family received a letter, only to know that his uncle was seriously ill in Guangzhou, and the family was very worried, especially his grandmother. How profound is the old lady's love for her son! So she asked Min'er's father to go to Guangzhou to visit his uncle. He went alone on Saturday morning.

Unknowingly, more than two weeks passed before his father returned from Guangzhou. The family was certainly very happy, because they had been looking forward to it for many days. They asked him if his uncle had recovered a little, how was the situation on the way? Was it calm? It was such a lively scene.

The next day, Min'er opened his mouth and asked his father: "Dad, did you go on a China Merchants Bureau ship? Did you go from the ocean?"

"I took a China Merchants Bureau ship in Shanghai, and when I left the Wusongkou, it was calm. The scenery at that time was really different from the scenery on land, especially when the sun was setting, it was particularly beautiful. Later, I passed through the East China Sea and arrived in Hong Kong, and then from Hong Kong to Guangzhou."

"The East China Sea must be very big. On this vast sea, how can the ship's helmsman know that this road is to Guangzhou?"

"The East China Sea is certainly very big, and beyond it is the Pacific Ocean. They must be very skilled in driving to be able to recognize a road to Guangzhou on the sea. Haven't you taken a small steamship? When the small steamship is sailing, isn't there a person called "老大" (Old Man) blocking a steering wheel on the bow to make the ship turn left and right? The big ship also has someone next to the steering wheel to steer. But the "老大" of the small steamship can freely turn the steering wheel according to the situation, while the person who steers the big ship must listen to the captain's orders and cannot turn it by himself. He only has to look at a compass in front, the compass is the compass, keeping the direction of the compass issued by the captain. Once the ship leaves the port, the captain issues the direction of the compass - it can also be called the compass course. This compass course is obtained from a very detailed map of the sea surface. This nautical chart records: the depth of the water, the nature of the seabed, whether it is mud, sand or rock, the height of the mountains, where there are reefs, and where there are lighthouses, are all recorded clearly, and there is also a direction map. The captain finds the safest and shortest route from the starting point to the destination on this nautical chart. Then he pushes the square foot to the direction map to measure its direction. In addition, the influence of the wind, tide, iron quality on the ship, and the difference between the Earth's magnetic pole and the north and south poles at that time and place, etc., so they sail on the sea in a certain direction from this compass course, but human knowledge and experience are limited after all, so there are often various errors."

Two Good Times in the Morning and Evening

—Fan Xianwei

During the day, children are in school, dang, dang, dang, class is over, with the passage of time, in form, from 9 am to open the schoolbag to 4 pm to leave school, even if the work of the day is over, in fact, where can it be considered finished, only the work in the classroom, the time is limited, not to mention that there are still unclear places, or have not been printed in the small brain?

Now the class uses a fractional system, usually each session is only 30 minutes, at most 40 minutes, in the blink of an eye, it is dang, dang, dang, class is over, to be honest: in the hours of class, several major subjects are almost entirely the students being instilled - listening to the lecture time, like a bottle filling water, the leakage and non-leakage of that water, is entirely up to you to pay attention and maintain! Because there is simply no chance to review "swallowing dates whole", how can you get practical benefits? It's like eating a delicious side dish, if you don't chew it in your mouth, the throat is over, isn't it going to be "the taste is lost immediately", so children should add some self-study efforts in addition to class, only then is the work finished, and get real knowledge!

What is the best time for self-study? "Morning" and "evening" are really the most appropriate, and getting up early every day can also improve physical health, the morning spirit and light are better, suitable for writing, calculation, etc., (at least one hour) in the evening, the electric light will damage eyesight, suitable for reading, doing diaries, doing handicrafts, etc., (also one hour) if you can do this without interruption for one day, the benefits are really immeasurable! Because two hours of self-study a day is sixty hours a month, and seven hundred and twenty hours a year, how great!

The Egg That Disobeys Orders

—Ziliang

Take an egg, pierce a hole at both ends of the egg, pour out the yolk and egg white, and mix iron powder and wax together at one end, heat it on the flame for a while to melt the wax in the egg and solidify the iron powder at one point, so that it cannot move. This egg that disobeys orders is made. If you want it to sleep, it just wants to stand up. If you want it to stand upside down, it just turns a somersault and stands upright again. If you draw a human figure on the egg, it will be a very interesting tumbler. You can also use this tumbler as a magic trick in front of your friends. You can say to your friends: "Everyone look! This egg is so disobedient. I want it to sleep, but it just won't sleep. Let me cast a spell to make it obey my orders."

As you say this, pick up the tumbler and bake it on the fire a few times to melt the wax in the egg. Then quickly shake the egg so that the iron powder and wax in the egg do not solidify on the eggshell.

After doing this work, you can say to your friends: "Okay, okay, now the tumbler obeys my orders! Everyone look, I want it to stand, it stands; I want it to sleep, it sleeps!"

If you play with skillful techniques, your friends will be surprised. This is also done by applying the center of gravity of the object. Children, why not try this game at home!

My Sister's Little Invention

—Xian Sheng

—How to Wash Away Stains in Bottles

Children, I will tell you a practical method; that is, how to wash away the stains in the bottle. This is a recent invention by one of my younger sisters, she dare not hide it, and asked me to write it out to tell you; I think the invention is not very important, but it is very practical, so I agreed to her and started writing about the process of her invention and this method. If you praise her for being clever after reading it, then my little sister will definitely feel happy and open her little mouth to smile at you.

It's like this, this half year she was promoted to the first grade of senior elementary school, the school stipulates that she must practice writing English letters, isn't that need to use blue ink? To buy a bottle of blue ink in the store costs eight copper plates, and it is a very small bottle, and it will be finished before long. My little sister is very economical, she bought five copper plates of indigo blue to dissolve herself, so she can dissolve a big bottle, enough for a semester, isn't that very cheap?

But after the indigo blue was dissolved, she found that there was no bottle to put it in, which made her embarrassed. Although there are many milk bottles and juice bottles, these bottles are not suitable, not only is it inconvenient to dip ink, but it is also very tiring to carry, and wouldn't she be laughed to death when she took it to school!

Later, she finally found a bottle of my used ink under the bookcase. This bottle used to hold red ink, so there were only red marks inside. She was very happy, and hurriedly washed it with water, but because the red marks had been around for a long time, they were stuck like paint, and it was not easy to remove. She wrapped a layer of cloth around a chopstick and stuffed it into the bottle to wipe, and the layer of marks on the bottom was removed by her, but the layer of marks around it still existed, because the bottle mouth was small and the chopsticks could not wipe it. This made her distressed again. She tried all kinds of methods, but none of them worked. When she was extremely distressed, she didn't know how she found a pile of fine sand on the ground in the corner. She had an idea and thought of putting these sands into the bottle, adding some water, and then shaking the bottle hard to make the sand rub inside, wouldn't it be possible to grind off the stains inside? She did as she did, and sure enough, in less than a moment, the bottle was washed brightly.

Children, if you encounter the same difficulties as my sister when washing bottles, you can do it in this way, I can guarantee you will succeed; because I have also tried it several times!

The Flying Technique of the Flying Fish

— Dong Xun

The flying fish is a very peculiar type of fish. In biology, its scientific name is Cypse'urus agoo, also known as the swallowtail flying fish. It is a type of marine fish belonging to the Ostariophysi order and is found in tropical and subtropical oceans. This flying fish is about one and a half feet long. What makes it most different and unique from other fish is that its pectoral fins are exceptionally large. Their front end almost reaches the base of the caudal fin. When opened, they resemble the wings of a monoplane, and their color is semi-transparent. The upper lobe of the caudal fin is larger, while the lower lobe is smaller. As for its pelvic fins, they are located almost before the anal fin, divided into two sizes. The larger pelvic fins resemble the rear wings of an airplane when flying, so they are called four-winged flying fish when combined with the pectoral fins. The smaller pelvic fins are only called two-winged flying fish. These two types can be said to be the main types of flying fish, because they, like other fish, are divided into many species.

The flying fish can be called a natural glider. It can fly out of the water at a speed of 50-70 per second and soar above the water's surface. When it is flying, its pectoral fins are very stable, unlike the wings of birds, which flap in the air during flight.

A biologist specializing in flying fish, Mr. Carl Hubbs—a researcher at the Zoological Institute of the University of Michigan—said after years of research that the flying fish's flying method is very unique. When they are about to fly out of the water, they fold their pectoral fins and move straight towards the surface of the water (A). The pectoral fins unfold as soon as they emerge from the water, and the front part of the fish's body flies out of the water (B). The lower lobe of the caudal fin strikes the water surface, generating the power to fly out of the water. Within one second, its caudal fin can strike 50 or even 70 times (C). When the pelvic fins unfold, the fish's body completely flies out of the water (D), and both pairs of fins (pectoral fins and pelvic fins) are fully unfolded. (This refers to the four-winged type of flying fish) (E). The flying time of the flying fish is extremely short, only half a minute, but sometimes they dip their caudal fins into the water, which allows them to take off again and continue flying above the water. The posture of the flying fish when entering the water is also very beautiful. It puts its pectoral fins together, makes a turn, and enters the water (F).

When flying, flying fish often make quick turns. Because of the excessive speed, they often bump into other fish or even boats. Sometimes they are hit by high waves. The posture of their flight, when viewed from a distance, looks like a semi-circular arc, which is really beautiful!

There are many interesting creatures in the ocean, and the flying fish is just one of them!

Filial Piety (2)

— Hai

The day arrived; she went to the whispering pine forest, praying to heaven to give her the courage to present this idea to her father and have him accept it well. But prayers are often not immediately effective. Her father quietly listened to her speech and then called his wife, saying, "Hey! Here comes a female benefactor! Our daughter is preparing to go to St. Petersburg to intercede with the emperor on our behalf." Then he told his wife about his daughter's plan. His heart was pounding, and his voice contained a joking tone.

His wife opened her mouth and said, "She should do her job properly and not say such senseless things." Poor Pascoffe was very upset when she heard this and couldn't help sobbing. Her mother handed her a cloth and said softly, "Dear, go wipe the table, prepare dinner, and then comfortably go to St. Petersburg."

Days passed like this, and Pascoffe brought up her idea again, asking her father to consider it. Her father became angry after being pestered and strictly forbade her to mention it again. She had no other way but to restrain herself; but for three consecutive years, she still prayed every day for the realization of her plan. During these three years, her mother had a serious illness that lasted a long time. Pascoffe took care of her while also managing the housework, gaining great trust from her parents. They no longer treated her as a child. When she brought up the old topic again, they no longer laughed at her, but earnestly advised her not to abandon them, because they were old and weak and couldn't do without her for a day, and it was very dangerous for her to go out alone on this long journey. She said nothing, but tears fell silently, but she couldn't abandon this long-standing plan.

But to set out, she had to have a passport, otherwise, she would be immediately sent back to Yizhi Village. Moreover, her father had submitted requests several times before, but they were all ignored. If he made any more requests, it would be the same useless. Fortunately, Pascoffe received help from an exiled official, who helped her apply for a passport. After waiting another six months, the reply came that she had not committed any crime, of course, she could freely leave Siberia, and the passport was sent. As soon as her father saw the passport, he snatched it and locked it up. He said that no matter how she begged, there would be no hope, so he was unwilling to let an eighteen-year-old girl go alone on this arduous journey.

Pascoffe still insisted on her idea, begging her mother every day to persuade her father to allow her to leave. In the end, her father couldn't resist her and finally softened. He said, "What are we going to do with this child? Since she is so determined to go, then we have no choice but to let her go." So he said to Pascoffe, "Poor child! Do you think that talking to the emperor in St. Petersburg is as easy as talking to your father in Siberia? His palace has soldiers guarding every gate, and you can't even cross the threshold. Moreover, we are as poor as beggars. You don't have good clothes to wear, and no one will introduce you. How are you going to see the emperor? And who will lead you into the palace?"

Telegraphic Special Issue

Shortwave

Interconnected Calls

— Lü Bing

In recent years, China's long-distance telephone business has been advancing rapidly. According to statistics released by the Ministry of Communications, the mileage of lines expanded each year is more than 10,000 kilometers. As a result, business has been opened in the east, calls have been completed in the west, and commercial ports, important cities, and even inland towns and cities can all make calls and communicate freely. The convenience for the public to use telephones is indeed improving day by day.

The Ministry of Communications' rapid development of telephones is due to the adoption of a phased construction method. The so-called phased construction means division of labor and cooperation. Therefore, once the plan is set, the construction teams proceed separately, carrying out construction and erection at the same time. As a result, the Beijing-Tongzhou section was completed soon, and the Tongzhou-Zhengzhou section was also completed. The Beijing-Hankou section was also completed soon after. Interconnected, all places along the line are connected. If so, then its construction is phased, but the result is still consistent, connected to each other, forming interconnected calls.

The result of interconnected calls can increase human interaction, shorten geographical distances, and save time. It has a significant contribution to the development of domestic industry and commerce. This point should be well known to anyone. Now that the country is in trouble and foreign aggression is imminent, even leaving aside industry and commerce, national unity, unified steps, and concerted efforts against foreign enemies are the urgent tasks at hand. China has a vast territory and abundant resources. Critics often say that it is like a plate of loose sand. The way to remedy this is to unite first. The construction of transportation is to promote domestic unity. Once the Beijing-Hankou line is open, the distance between Beijing and Hankou is as close as neighbors. If there is another transfer, then the provinces of Henan, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, etc., will also respond quickly. In this way, the whole country will be tightened invisibly, the land will be concentrated, making the interaction between people closer, and the connection between the central government and local governments closer, enhancing mutual relations, and enriching the strength of unity. This is the inherent meaning of interconnected calls.

Once the interconnected calls of various provinces are open, the connection between various provinces is also established. When we use this telephone to talk to people in any province, we feel that each other's voices are clear, and the communication is pleasant and seamless. In the past, mountains and rivers were obstructed, and communication was difficult. Now, speech can be heard, as if face-to-face. If we think deeply, we are indeed a family across the country. Sincerity can be achieved, and we cannot help but feel a sense of love and unity.

The Executive Yuan Actively Rectifies Official Telegraph Fees

— Zhen

Approved Three Relief Measures, Hoping that Heads of Political and Military Institutions Will Pay Attention

In order to rectify the charging of official and military telegrams, the Ministry of Communications submitted a proposal to the Executive Yuan to implement it earnestly from July 1 of this year, and also attached three rectification measures for official and military telegrams, printed and posted notices. At the same time, it notified all telegraph offices that they should strictly follow the order of the Executive Yuan and strictly implement it. Thereafter, official and military telegrams should be charged in cash according to regulations, and there should be no leniency.

Since the implementation of the above measures, most institutions have paid fees according to regulations, but there are still a few bureaus that have failed to do so due to financial difficulties or budget constraints. Regarding this point, the Ministry of Communications has jointly formulated three relief measures with the Ministries of Finance and Military Affairs, as follows:

(1) All institutions sending telegrams from July 1, 1936, should pay cash according to the revised regulations on the charging and restriction of official and military telegrams. All institutions, schools, and troops under the Military Affairs Commission and the Ministry of Military Affairs that fail to comply shall be responsible for collecting the arrears by the commission and the ministry. If other institutions fail to pay the required amount of telegraph fees due to the 1936 budget already being distributed, they should state the reasons and report to their respective competent authorities for verification. If verified to be true, they may be allowed to use the funds comprehensively within the original budget of the institution, or find other ways to increase funding to compensate for the arrears.

(2) Telecommunications is an important national undertaking. If it is not thoroughly rectified, it will have a great impact on politics and military affairs! Rectification and maintenance require funds everywhere. If various institutions do not strictly comply with the payment methods, not only is rectification hopeless, but there is also the risk of collapse! All institutions must comply with the regulations. If they fail to comply again, the telegraph office may stop sending their telegrams.

(3) Sending telegrams should not be excessive. Unless it is an emergency, fast mail should be used instead of sending telegrams at every turn. The text of the telegram should also be as concise as possible and not be lengthy.

The above three measures have been submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and forwarded to the National Government, ordering all directly subordinate institutions to comply and issuing separate orders. While we are grateful to the government for its painstaking efforts to maintain telecommunications, we should also clarify the three measures, hoping that heads of political and military institutions will pay attention to them!

1. Political and Military Institutions Should Maintain Telecommunications: Telecommunications is one of the transportation undertakings, which is of great importance to politics and military affairs. Daily maintenance depends on the income from telegraph fees. According to statistics, official and military telegrams sent by political and military institutions account for more than 60% of the annual number of telegrams. If the fees for these more than 60% of official telegrams cannot be fully collected, then the only thing to rely on to maintain telecommunications is the commercial telegram fees of less than 40% of the number of words. Telecommunications funds will naturally feel insufficient. It is also found that the annual arrears of official telegraph fees owed by political and military institutions are always more than 3 million yuan. If this huge amount of arrears is not remedied, not only is telecommunications construction hopeless, but there is also the risk of complete collapse! The impact will not only affect public communication but also military transportation, which will almost be cut off! In order to maintain telecommunications, the telegraph office has to comply with the order of the Executive Yuan to stop sending telegrams for institutions that do not pay fees according to regulations.

2. Political and Military Institutions Should Pay Fees According to Regulations: In the past, various institutions had limited funds due to budget reasons, and the amount of telegraph fees could not be determined. Once they are asked to pay fees according to regulations, there will be various difficulties. Now that the Executive Yuan has issued this order, if the amount of telegraph fees listed in the 1936 budget of various institutions is insufficient, they may state the reasons and report to their respective competent authorities for verification, allowing them to use the funds comprehensively within the budget of the institution, or find other ways to increase funding. Since the budget scope of various institutions has been expanded, telegraph funds can be said to be sufficient. Therefore, telegrams should be paid according to regulations to fulfill their responsibilities and cannot be excused by financial difficulties or insufficient budgets.

3. Political and Military Institutions Should Save on Telegraph Fees: Since there are the above-mentioned relief measures for telegraph fees for political and military institutions, there is certainly no problem. However, in order to maintain the budget, it is necessary to restrict sending telegrams. Only by restricting sending telegrams can we save on telegraph fees, and only by saving on telegraph fees can we maintain the budget. There are two ways to restrict sending telegrams: (1) Do not send telegrams unless it is an emergency; (2) The text of the telegram should be as short and concise as possible and not be lengthy. The former reduces the number of telegrams sent, and the latter reduces the number of words sent. If the number of times and the number of words are reduced, the telegraph fees will naturally be saved. Moreover, by saving the cost of unnecessary telegrams, there will be no arrears in telegraph fees due to insufficient budget when necessary telegrams are sent. Therefore, there is much room for research when considering the gains and losses.

The above three items, on the one hand, clarify the results of the Executive Yuan's approval of the three measures, and on the other hand, state the responsibilities of political and military institutions in maintaining telecommunications. Maintaining telecommunications is to maintain the Executive Yuan's orders and the ability of the political and military institutions themselves. I think that wise heads of political and military institutions will not dismiss these words.

General Description of Types of Long-Distance Telephone Calls

— Bao Zhen

The recently revised Domestic Long-Distance Telephone Business Regulations of the Ministry of Communications will be implemented from December 1 of this year. The names of various types of calls stipulated in the new regulations have been changed and are different from the current names. The comparison is as follows:

Original Name　Changed Name

Ordinary Call　Ordinary Dialing

Express Call　Express Dialing

Ordinary Notification　Ordinary Calling for Person

Express Notification　Express Calling for Person

Ordinary Call　Ordinary Paging

Express Call　Express Paging

Reserved Call　Scheduled Call

The new regulations divide long-distance telephone calls into the following three types:

1. Dialing Call: A call in which the caller dials the telephone number of a certain place without specifying a certain person to answer the call is called a dialing call. For example, "Nanjing—22450."

2. Calling for Person Call: A call in which the caller dials the telephone number of a certain place and specifies a certain person to answer the call, or specifies a certain user of a shared telephone, a certain extension of a private small exchange, or a certain part of a store or institution to talk to, is called a calling for person call. For example, "Tianjin 51847 Zhuang Yongfa." In addition to specifying A as the recipient, the caller may also specify B as the representative of the recipient, or specify another telephone number of the recipient for substitution. For example, "Tianjin 51847 Zhuang Yongfa or Cheng Bao Ying," "Tianjin 32239 or 32241 Ma Guozhang."

In various stores, residences, schools, apartments, institutions, etc. in China, the local telephones are usually answered by servants who then call the owner or other person in charge to answer the call. Because it requires a transfer, it inevitably takes a little time. If this is done, there is no time limit for local calls, and there is no economic loss. However, for long-distance telephone calls, if we use dialing calls, according to regulations, the time is charged from the time when the calling exchange connects to a certain telephone number in a certain place and the receiving user starts talking to the caller. Therefore, if the call is answered by the servant of the receiving user, and then the owner or other person in charge is called to talk, and the time spent is one or two minutes, and the talking time exceeds three minutes, then another charge must be paid, which is a great waste of money. However, for calling for person calls, according to regulations, the time is charged from the time when the recipient, or his representative, or a certain extension of the specified private small exchange, or a certain part of the specified store or institution, starts talking to the caller. Therefore, it does not waste time and money because of the transfer. Therefore, if long-distance callers know that the other party's telephone is for public use, or is usually answered by servants, it is better to use calling for person calls, which are faster and more economical, than to waste time and money due to the transfer.

3. Paging Call: A call in which the caller calls for a certain person in a certain place, but the recipient does not have a telephone, and the receiving telegraph office has to send a messenger to call the recipient to the telegraph office, or specify the nearest long-distance telephone retail store, or public telephone office to talk to, is called a paging call. For example, "Beiping Wu Yiku No. 13 Ye Yao Cheng." In addition to specifying A as the recipient, the caller may also specify another person as the representative of the recipient, so that if the recipient is not there, the representative will go to contact him. However, this representative of the recipient is limited to those who live in the same place as the recipient. For example, "Beiping Wu Yiku No. 13 Ye Yao Cheng or Lu Wen De."

The above three types of calls are divided into ordinary and express. All three types of calls for dialing, calling for person, and paging that are made in the order of registration are called ordinary calls. If the caller requests that the long-distance telephone calls he has made be put before other ordinary calls to connect the line, or notify the receiving telegraph office to send a messenger to call the recipient to the telephone to talk, they are called express calls. The locations where express dialing, express calling for person, and ordinary or express paging calls are open are determined by the Ministry of Communications and then announced by various telegraph offices. Paging calls are limited to recipients within the business area of the telegraph office, and those who have not specified a business area are limited to 3 kilometers from the office. According to the current long-distance telephone business regulations, a special fee must be added to the paging notification in addition to the call fee, and one-third of the call fee must be added to the advance notification. After the new regulations are implemented, the same fee will be charged for the above-mentioned calling for person and paging calls, and the special fee or the additional one-third call fee will be canceled. This new regulation is slightly different from the current price, and long-distance telephone users should pay special attention to it.

In addition to the above-mentioned ordinary and express calls, there are also the following three types of special calls in the new regulations:

1. Special Call: If the caller needs to talk to a certain person in a certain place between two specified telephones at a fixed time of day for a fixed period of time, it is called a special call. The above-mentioned special calls are very convenient for major commercial firms to report commercial market conditions. However, the registration period must be at least one month, and the call fee must be paid in advance by the applicant. The applicant and the telegraph office must sign a contract to ensure good faith.

2. Scheduled Call: A long-distance telephone call that is pre-scheduled for a call time within the business hours stipulated by the telegraph office when the caller registers is called a scheduled call. However, this scheduled call must be registered several hours in advance before the scheduled call time, and the time is determined and announced by the telegraph office.

For the above two types of special calls and scheduled calls, if the long-distance line is already occupied when the scheduled call time arrives, it should be connected after the already connected telephone call is completed.

3. Night Call: A long-distance telephone call that is made from a certain time to a certain time at night, and the call price is lower than the daytime call price, is called a night call. This call is very convenient for news reporters to transmit news, and it is also cheap.

The locations for the above three types and other special long-distance telephone businesses are determined by the Telecommunications Administration in accordance with actual needs and the complexity of the lines and submitted to the Ministry of Communications for approval. The detailed methods and prices are regulated separately. As for the registration procedures, call order, and billing methods for using long-distance telephones, they are not within the scope of this article, and I will talk about them in another article.

Explanation on the Supplementary Collection of Address Fees

— Chao Ao

A telegram that uses an expired registered address instead of the recipient's name and address will be stopped from being delivered according to regulations. In order to facilitate the public, the Ministry of Communications has previously formulated a lenient measure. If there is such a telegram, the address fee will be supplemented, and it will still be delivered. This was originally a lenient measure to facilitate the public. However, it has often caused misunderstandings recently. The reasons for the misunderstanding are nothing more than the following: (1) Sometimes the recipient does not have money on hand and asks the telegraph office messenger to deliver the telegram first and pay the address fee later. The messenger refuses, and the recipient is anxious to see the telegram, which causes a misunderstanding. (2) Sometimes the recipient delays taking the money for too long, and the messenger urges, which causes a misunderstanding. Now let me explain them separately:

Regarding item (1), the telegraph office originally respected the recipient's wishes, and the messenger used to do so. Later, because there were several disputes, some recipients refused to pay the address fee after reading the telegram, and some said that the telegram was not theirs after reading it and refused to pay the fee. The messenger had to pay the address fee back because the telegram had been opened. From then on, the messenger refused to deliver the telegram first. However, because of the dishonesty of one or two people, the vast majority of trustworthy recipients felt inconvenienced. In order to remedy this shortcoming, the telegraph office is researching remedial measures to make it convenient for the public who have always been trustworthy. However, it is best to hope that registered recipients will go to the telegraph office to renew their registration before the registration expires to avoid the loss of paying the address fee.

Regarding item (2), the telegraph office has a limited return time for messengers to deliver telegrams in order to avoid delaying the telegrams. If there is a delay, there will be punishment. Therefore, if the messenger has to wait for a long time, he will feel that there are difficulties in his work. I hope that the recipients will forgive this.

In short, the occurrence of misunderstandings is often that neither party is wrong, but just some small gaps. Once explained clearly, they will be resolved!

Radio Programs and Children's Education

— Xu Weili

—Solving a Difficult Problem for All Parents—

I once read in a Shanghai newspaper: "Although Shanghai's radio stations are highly developed, the programs broadcast cater mostly to base and vulgar tastes, which has a significant impact on children's lives. Most stories involve mythology and even absurd fabrications, which not only fail to assist children's education but also harm children's minds. Therefore, many parents have specially made wooden boxes to lock up the radio as soon as their children come home from school to prevent them from listening."

We express our sympathy to all parents who care for their children and see this as a sign of progress in family education in China today, where parents are paying close attention to their children's education. We sincerely hope that all radio stations across the country can understand the parents' painstaking efforts in education and broadcast programs beneficial to children as much as possible during after-school hours to assist in children's education.

Now, there is good news to share with all parents: the Shanghai Radio Station of the Ministry of Communications, based on supplementing social education and promoting wholesome entertainment in the family, has specially established a children's program, with many children's education experts in charge of broadcasting children's stories, etc. This is to enhance children's knowledge, learn the national language, and hone their eloquence. Listening to it after school will surely achieve twice the result with half the effort in children's education. Furthermore, children will no longer seek other harmful entertainment when they hear interesting educational stories. All families with wireless radios are invited to listen to the educational programs broadcast by the Shanghai Radio Station of the Ministry of Communications at a frequency of 1300 and a call sign of XOHC, which will surely satisfy you.

Recently, the station has been broadcasting children's programs (daily from 6:30 PM to 7:00 PM) (except Sundays). They have specially invited Ms. Hu Ying, a former children's education expert from Peking University, to tell the story of "The Hardships and Efforts of a Poor Boy," briefly recounting the story of a poor boy who was originally a descendant of a noble family but was dispossessed and abandoned by his uncle. He was later adopted and, at the age of ten or so, wandered around with a street performer. Eventually, by chance, he met his mother and younger brother, who was very ill. Unfortunately, they were soon separated again. After the separation, the poor boy continued his wandering life, experiencing many difficulties and dangers, and finally reunited with his mother and brother, eventually becoming a great man. The plot is full of twists and turns, and the writing is lively. Ms. Hu tells it vividly, and children will surely be interested in listening. We hope all wise parents will pay attention to it.
